# 16-Week HYROX Preparation Plan — Complete Programming Engine

> **Athlete Profile:** Male, 35–40 mpw running base, 4–5 strength sessions/week, transitioning 2–3 strength sessions to HIIT/hybrid work. Target race: June 6, 2025. Training start: ~February 17, 2025.

---

## 1. Macro-Level Periodization Structure

### 1.1 Phase Overview

| Phase | Weeks | Dates | Primary Goal | Running Volume | Strength Sessions | HIIT/Hyrox Sessions | Hyrox Simulations |
|-------|-------|-------|-------------|---------------|-------------------|--------------------|--------------------|
| **Phase 1: General Prep** | 1–4 | Feb 17 – Mar 16 | Build aerobic engine, introduce Hyrox movements, establish baseline benchmarks | 35–38 mpw | 2/week | 2/week | 0 (benchmark testing only) |
| **Phase 2: Specific Prep** | 5–8 | Mar 17 – Apr 13 | Develop station-specific capacity, increase HIIT density, introduce compromised running | 36–40 mpw | 2/week | 3/week | 1 (half-sim in Week 8) |
| **Phase 3: Competition Prep** | 9–12 | Apr 14 – May 11 | Race-pace simulation, pacing discipline, peak HIIT complexity, refine weaknesses | 35–38 mpw | 1–2/week | 3/week | 2 (Weeks 10, 12) |
| **Phase 4: Taper & Peak** | 13–16 | May 12 – Jun 6 | Reduce volume, maintain intensity, sharpen race-day execution, mental prep | 28–32 mpw (↓20–25%) | 1/week | 2/week (reduced volume) | 1 (Week 14, dress rehearsal) |

### 1.2 Deload Weeks

Every 4th week is a **deload week** (Weeks 4, 8, 12). During deload:
- Running volume drops 20–25%
- HIIT session count drops from 3 → 2, with reduced volume per session (cut sets by 30–40%)
- Strength intensity maintained at 85–90% of working loads but volume halved (2 sets instead of 4)
- No race simulations during deload
- Add one extra rest or active recovery day

Week 16 is the final taper/race week — treated as a super-deload.

### 1.3 Weekly Volume Progression Table

| Week | Phase | Running (miles) | Runs/wk | Strength Sessions | HIIT Sessions | Simulation | Total Training Days |
|------|-------|----------------|---------|-------------------|---------------|------------|---------------------|
| 1 | GP | 35 | 5 | 2 | 2 | — | 6 |
| 2 | GP | 36 | 5 | 2 | 2 | — | 6 |
| 3 | GP | 38 | 5 | 2 | 2 | — | 6 |
| 4 | GP (Deload) | 30 | 4 | 2 (½ vol) | 2 (½ vol) | Benchmark Test | 5 |
| 5 | SP | 37 | 5 | 2 | 3 | — | 6 |
| 6 | SP | 38 | 5 | 2 | 3 | — | 6 |
| 7 | SP | 40 | 5 | 2 | 3 | — | 6 |
| 8 | SP (Deload) | 32 | 4 | 2 (½ vol) | 2 (½ vol) | Half-Sim | 5 |
| 9 | CP | 37 | 5 | 2 | 3 | — | 6 |
| 10 | CP | 38 | 5 | 1 | 3 | Full Sim | 6 |
| 11 | CP | 36 | 5 | 2 | 3 | — | 6 |
| 12 | CP (Deload) | 30 | 4 | 1 (½ vol) | 2 (½ vol) | ¾ Sim | 5 |
| 13 | Taper | 32 | 4 | 1 | 2 | — | 5 |
| 14 | Taper | 30 | 4 | 1 | 2 | Dress Rehearsal (½ sim) | 5 |
| 15 | Taper | 28 | 4 | 1 (light) | 1 (short/sharp) | — | 4 |
| 16 | Race Week | 15 | 3 (short) | 0 | 0 | **RACE DAY** | 3 + Race |

### 1.4 How Key Variables Evolve Across Phases

| Variable | Phase 1 (GP) | Phase 2 (SP) | Phase 3 (CP) | Phase 4 (Taper) |
|----------|-------------|-------------|-------------|----------------|
| **Running intensity mix** | 80% Zone 2, 10% tempo, 10% intervals | 75% Z2, 10% tempo, 15% intervals + compromised | 70% Z2, 10% tempo, 20% intervals + compromised | 75% Z2, 25% short sharp work |
| **Sled weight** | 80% race weight (122 kg) | 90% race weight (137 kg) | 100% race weight (152 kg) | 100% race weight, reduced reps |
| **Wall ball reps per HIIT set** | 50–75 | 75–100 | 100 (full race reps) | 50–75 (maintenance) |
| **BBJ distance per session** | 40 m | 60 m | 80 m (full race distance) | 40 m |
| **Strength rep ranges** | 4–6 reps @ 80–85% 1RM | 6–10 reps @ 70–80% 1RM | 8–12 reps @ 65–75% 1RM | 4–6 reps @ 75–80% 1RM (neural maintenance) |
| **HIIT time domains** | 10–15 min pieces | 15–25 min pieces | 20–40 min pieces | 8–15 min pieces |
| **Rest periods (HIIT)** | 1:1 to 1:2 work:rest | 1:0.75 to 1:1 | 1:0.5 to 1:1 | 1:1 to 1:2 |

## 2. Weekly Templates by Phase

### 2.1 Phase 1: General Preparation (Weeks 1–3; Week 4 = Deload)

**Intent:** Build aerobic base, introduce all 8 Hyrox station movements at sub-race loads, establish movement patterns and baseline benchmarks. Running dominates. Strength remains heavy but transitioning from bodybuilding to functional patterns.

| Day | Session Type | Duration | Key Focus / Intent | Example Workout |
|-----|-------------|----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** | Easy Run (AM) + HIIT (PM) | 50 min + 45 min | Zone 2 aerobic base; introduce SkiErg/Row pacing | AM: 6 mi easy @ 8:00–8:30/mi. PM: HIIT #1 (Erg Pacing Builder) |
| **Tuesday** | Strength | 60 min | Lower body strength: squat and hinge patterns | Back Squat 4×5 @ 80% 1RM, RDL 3×8, Walking Lunge 3×12/leg, Calf Raises 3×15. Rest 2–3 min between squat sets. |
| **Wednesday** | Tempo Run | 55 min | Lactate threshold development | 2 mi warm-up → 3 mi @ half-marathon pace (threshold) → 2 mi cool-down. Total: 7 mi. |
| **Thursday** | HIIT (Hyrox Stations) | 50 min | Station skill development: sled + wall ball introduction | HIIT #2 (Station Introduction Circuit) |
| **Friday** | Easy Run | 45 min | Recovery-pace aerobic volume | 5.5 mi easy @ 8:30–9:00/mi, fully conversational |
| **Saturday** | Long Run + Strength (PM optional) | 75 min + 45 min | Aerobic endurance; upper body strength | AM: 10 mi easy @ 8:00–8:30/mi. PM: Bench Press 4×6, Barbell Row 4×8, Strict Press 3×8, Pull-ups 3×max. |
| **Sunday** | Rest / Active Recovery | 30 min max | Full recovery, mobility | 20 min walk + 10 min foam roll/stretch. Optional: yoga. |

**Weekly mileage: ~35.5 mi** (6 + 7 + 5.5 + 10 + 3×short warm-up/cool-down mi within HIIT = ~35–36)

---

### 2.2 Phase 2: Specific Preparation (Weeks 5–7; Week 8 = Deload)

**Intent:** Increase Hyrox station loads toward race weight, introduce compromised running (running immediately after station work), add a third HIIT session, begin reducing strength session volume while maintaining intensity.

| Day | Session Type | Duration | Key Focus / Intent | Example Workout |
|-----|-------------|----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** | Easy Run (AM) + HIIT (PM) | 50 min + 50 min | Aerobic base; sled push/pull at 90% race weight | AM: 6 mi easy. PM: HIIT #5 (Sled Power Endurance) |
| **Tuesday** | Strength + Short Run | 55 min + 25 min | Lower body strength-endurance; compromised running intro | Strength: Front Squat 3×8 @ 72%, DB Walking Lunge 3×10/leg @ 30 kg DBs, GHD Back Extension 3×12, Farmer Hold 3×45 sec heavy. Then: 2.5 mi easy run immediately after (compromised). |
| **Wednesday** | Interval Run | 60 min | VO₂max development (Norwegian 4×4) | 2 mi warm-up → 4×4 min @ 90% HRmax w/ 3 min jog recovery → 2 mi cool-down. Total: ~8 mi. |
| **Thursday** | HIIT (Hyrox Full-Body) | 55 min | Wall balls, BBJ, lunges at increasing loads | HIIT #8 (The Grinder: BBJ + Wall Ball + Lunge Chipper) |
| **Friday** | Easy Run | 45 min | Recovery volume | 5.5 mi easy @ 8:15–8:45/mi |
| **Saturday** | Long Run (AM) + HIIT (PM) | 80 min + 45 min | Endurance + station practice under fatigue | AM: 11 mi easy (last 2 mi at tempo). PM: HIIT #10 (Compromised Running Circuit) |
| **Sunday** | Rest / Active Recovery | 30 min | Full recovery | Walk, foam roll, light mobility |

**Weekly mileage: ~38.5 mi** (6 + 2.5 + 8 + 5.5 + 11 + ~5.5 from HIIT run components)

---

### 2.3 Phase 3: Competition Preparation (Weeks 9–11; Week 12 = Deload)

**Intent:** Race-weight stations, full-distance station work, race-pace simulation sessions, pacing refinement, mental toughness development. Running volume holds steady but intensity of HIIT peaks. One strength session drops to maintenance-only.

| Day | Session Type | Duration | Key Focus / Intent | Example Workout |
|-----|-------------|----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** | Easy Run (AM) + HIIT (PM) | 50 min + 55 min | Aerobic base; race-weight sled + erg intervals | AM: 6 mi easy. PM: HIIT #12 (Race Pace Station Intervals) |
| **Tuesday** | Strength (Maintenance) | 50 min | Lower body neural maintenance; heavy but low volume | Back Squat 3×4 @ 82%, Deadlift 3×3 @ 85%, Single-Leg RDL 2×8/leg, Hanging Knee Raise 3×12. Rest 3 min between compound sets. |
| **Wednesday** | Tempo/Threshold Run | 60 min | Race-pace running with negative split practice | 2 mi warm-up → 4 mi at goal Hyrox run pace (4:30–4:45/km) → 1 mi at 10 sec/km faster → 1 mi cool-down. Total: ~8 mi. |
| **Thursday** | HIIT (Hyrox Race-Specific) | 60 min | Full-distance stations under fatigue, compromised running | HIIT #14 (4-Station Hyrox Block) |
| **Friday** | Easy Run | 40 min | Recovery | 5 mi easy |
| **Saturday** | HIIT/Simulation (AM) + Short Run (PM) | 70 min + 25 min | Hyrox simulation (full or partial); benchmark tracking | Full Sim #2 or HIIT #16 (depending on week). PM: 3 mi easy shakeout. |
| **Sunday** | Rest / Active Recovery | 30 min | Full recovery | Walk, stretch, mental visualization |

**Weekly mileage: ~37 mi** (6 + 8 + 5 + 3 + ~15 from within HIIT/sim sessions)

---

### 2.4 Phase 4: Taper & Peak (Weeks 13–16)

**Intent:** Volume drops 20–30%. Intensity maintained on key sessions. Sharpen race execution, practice pacing, build confidence, arrive race day fresh and fast.

#### Weeks 13–14 Template

| Day | Session Type | Duration | Key Focus / Intent | Example Workout |
|-----|-------------|----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** | Easy Run + HIIT (PM) | 45 min + 40 min | Maintain aerobic base; short, sharp HIIT | AM: 5 mi easy. PM: HIIT #17 (Taper Sharpener — 15-min EMOM with reduced volume) |
| **Tuesday** | Strength (Light Maintenance) | 40 min | Neural activation, not fatigue | Back Squat 2×4 @ 78%, RDL 2×6 @ 70%, Pull-ups 2×8, Plank 2×45 sec. |
| **Wednesday** | Interval Run (Reduced) | 50 min | VO₂max maintenance at reduced volume | 2 mi warm-up → 3×4 min @ 90% HRmax w/ 3 min jog → 2 mi cool-down. Total: ~7 mi. |
| **Thursday** | HIIT (Race-Pace Touchpoint) or Dress Rehearsal (Wk 14) | 45–60 min | Race-pace stations at reduced volume; OR Half-Simulation | Wk 13: HIIT #19 (Race-Pace Express). Wk 14: Simulation #5 (Dress Rehearsal). |
| **Friday** | Easy Run | 35 min | Legs-up recovery jog | 4 mi easy |
| **Saturday** | Easy Run | 50 min | Long(er) easy effort, last before final taper | 6 mi easy |
| **Sunday** | Rest | — | Full rest | — |

**Weekly mileage: ~30 mi**

#### Week 15 Template

| Day | Session Type | Duration | Key Focus / Intent | Example Workout |
|-----|-------------|----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** | Easy Run | 40 min | Aerobic maintenance | 5 mi easy |
| **Tuesday** | HIIT (Short & Sharp) | 30 min | Race-pace touch — reduced volume, high quality | HIIT #20 (Race Primer — 10-min EMOM, race-weight stations, 50% volume) |
| **Wednesday** | Easy Run + 4×Strides | 35 min | Neuromuscular activation | 4 mi easy + 4×100m strides @ mile pace w/ walk-back |
| **Thursday** | Rest or Light Walk | 20 min | Recovery | 20-min walk + mobility |
| **Friday** | Easy Run | 30 min | Shakeout | 3.5 mi easy |
| **Saturday** | Rest | — | Full rest | — |
| **Sunday** | Rest or Light Walk | 20 min | Pre-race week transition | Walk + visualization |

**Weekly mileage: ~15.5 mi**

#### Week 16 — Race Week

| Day | Session Type | Duration | Key Focus / Intent | Example Workout |
|-----|-------------|----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** (Jun 2) | Easy Run + Strides | 30 min | Last real workout before race | 3 mi easy + 4×80m strides. Gentle. Controlled. |
| **Tuesday** (Jun 3) | Rest or 15-min Walk | 15 min | Full recovery | Optional: 15 min walk + light stretching. |
| **Wednesday** (Jun 4) | Shakeout Run | 20 min | Neural priming, confidence builder | 2 mi easy with 2×30-sec race-pace pickups. |
| **Thursday** (Jun 5) | Rest | — | Pre-race rest, gear prep, mental visualization | Pack race bag, write pacing targets on arm, prep nutrition (gels, electrolytes). |
| **Friday** (Jun 6) | **RACE DAY** | ~70–90 min | Execute race plan | Full warm-up protocol (see Section 6). |
| **Saturday** (Jun 7) | Active Recovery | 20 min | Post-race recovery | Walk, light stretching, high-carb + protein meal. |
| **Sunday** (Jun 8) | Rest | — | Full rest | — |

## 3. HIIT Session Library (20 Workouts)

Each workout is fully prescribed with movements, sets, reps, intensity, rest periods, time caps, scaling options, and target scores. Workouts are numbered #1–#20 and organized by phase deployment.

---

### HIIT #1 — Erg Pacing Builder (Phase 1)
**Format:** Alternating EMOM  
**Duration:** 20 minutes (20 rounds)  
**Target:** SkiErg + Row pacing discipline; aerobic capacity  
**Equipment:** SkiErg, Concept2 RowErg

| Minute | Movement | Prescription | Target |
|--------|----------|-------------|--------|
| Odd minutes (1,3,5…) | SkiErg | 15 calories | Complete in ~40 sec, rest remainder |
| Even minutes (2,4,6…) | Row | 15 calories | Complete in ~42 sec, rest remainder |

**Intensity:** RPE 6–7. Aim for identical split each round (±1 sec). If you finish with <12 sec rest, reduce to 12 cal.  
**Scaling:** Reduce to 12 cal per round (beginner) or increase to 18 cal (advanced).  
**Target Score:** Total calories should be 300 (15×20). Track deviation from target split each round.

---

### HIIT #2 — Station Introduction Circuit (Phase 1)
**Format:** 4 Rounds For Quality (not for time)  
**Duration:** 40–45 minutes  
**Target:** Movement skill acquisition for all 8 Hyrox stations at sub-race loads

| Round | Movement | Prescription | Notes |
|-------|----------|-------------|-------|
| A | SkiErg | 250 m @ controlled pace | Focus on lat engagement, hip hinge |
| B | Sled Push | 2 × 12.5 m @ 80% race weight (122 kg) | Practice 45° body angle, short steps |
| C | Sled Pull | 2 × 12.5 m @ 80% race weight (82 kg) | Practice hip extension technique |
| D | Burpee Broad Jump | 20 m | Step-up method, consistent jump distance |
| E | Row | 250 m @ controlled pace | 24–26 spm, legs-back-arms sequence |
| F | Farmers Carry | 50 m @ 2×24 kg | Tall posture, brisk walk |
| G | Sandbag Lunges | 25 m @ 20 kg | 0.9–1.0 m step length, touch-and-go |
| H | Wall Balls | 25 reps @ 6 kg to 10 ft | Full squat depth, catch-and-squat rhythm |

**Rest:** 60–90 sec between stations. Walk to next station = transition practice.  
**Scaling:** Reduce loads by 20% or cut distances/reps in half for beginners. Advanced: race weight on everything, reduce rest to 30 sec.

---

### HIIT #3 — Norwegian 4×4 on the Rower (Phase 1)
**Format:** Interval  
**Duration:** 30 minutes  
**Target:** VO₂max development, rowing pacing discipline

| Set | Prescription | Intensity | Rest |
|-----|-------------|-----------|------|
| Warm-up | 5 min easy row @ 2:15–2:30/500m | Zone 2 | — |
| Interval 1 | 4 min row @ 85–90% HRmax (target 1:50–1:55/500m) | Zone 4–5 | 3 min easy row |
| Interval 2 | 4 min row | Same | 3 min easy row |
| Interval 3 | 4 min row | Same | 3 min easy row |
| Interval 4 | 4 min row | Same | — |
| Cool-down | 3 min easy row | Zone 1 | — |

**Target Score:** Total meters rowed during the 4 work intervals. Track each 4-min distance individually — variance >30m between intervals = pacing failure.  
**Scaling:** Reduce to 3×4 min if RPE exceeds 9/10 on interval 3. Advanced: add 5th interval.

---

### HIIT #4 — Wall Ball Endurance Builder (Phase 1)
**Format:** EMOM 16  
**Duration:** 16 minutes  
**Target:** Muscular endurance for wall balls; pacing across high-rep sets

| Minute | Movement | Prescription |
|--------|----------|-------------|
| Min 1–4 | Wall Balls | 15 reps @ 6 kg to 10 ft target |
| Min 5–8 | Air Squat | 15 reps (tempo: 2-sec down, explosive up) |
| Min 9–12 | Wall Balls | 15 reps @ 6 kg |
| Min 13–16 | Wall Balls | 12 reps @ 6 kg |

**Rest:** Remainder of each minute. Target: complete wall balls in 35–45 sec per set, leaving 15–25 sec rest.  
**Intensity:** RPE 7 by round 12. If RPE > 8 by round 8, reduce to 12 reps per set.  
**Total reps:** 162 wall balls + 60 air squats.  
**Scaling:** Reduce to 10 wall balls per set (beginner). Advanced: 20 reps per set or use 9 kg ball.

---

### HIIT #5 — Sled Power Endurance (Phase 2)
**Format:** Every 3:00 × 8 Sets  
**Duration:** 24 minutes  
**Target:** Sled push/pull at race or near-race weight; sustained output with controlled rest

| Set | Movement | Prescription | Notes |
|-----|----------|-------------|-------|
| 1 | Sled Push | 4 × 12.5 m (50m) @ 137 kg (90% race weight) | Continuous — never let sled stop |
| 2 | Sled Pull | 4 × 12.5 m (50m) @ 93 kg (90% race weight) | Hip extension method, rapid hand-over-hand |
| 3 | Sled Push | 50m @ 137 kg | Same cues |
| 4 | Sled Pull | 50m @ 93 kg | Same cues |
| 5 | Sled Push | 50m @ 137 kg | Push pace — aim to beat Set 1 time |
| 6 | Sled Pull | 50m @ 93 kg | Same |
| 7 | Sled Push | 50m @ 137 kg | — |
| 8 | Sled Pull | 50m @ 93 kg | — |

**Rest:** Remaining time in the 3:00 window. Aim for 90–120 sec work per set, leaving 60–90 sec rest.  
**Intensity:** RPE 7–8. Track split times for each 50m — variance >10 sec across sets = poor pacing.  
**Scaling:** Reduce to 80% race weight (122 kg push / 82 kg pull) if failing to complete in <2:00. Advanced: 100% race weight (152 kg / 103 kg).

---

### HIIT #6 — Burpee Broad Jump + Run Coupling (Phase 2)
**Format:** 5 Rounds For Time  
**Duration:** 20–28 minutes (time cap: 30 min)  
**Target:** BBJ pacing, compromised running

| Round | Movement | Prescription |
|-------|----------|-------------|
| Each round | Burpee Broad Jump | 16 m (step-up method, ~10–12 reps) |
| Then | Run | 400 m @ goal Hyrox run pace (4:30–4:45/km = ~1:48–1:54 per 400m) |

**Rest:** None between movements. Walk 30 sec between rounds only if RPE ≥ 9.  
**Intensity:** RPE 7–8. BBJ should take ~60–75 sec per 16m. Run pacing is critical — use GPS watch.  
**Target time:** 22–26 min total. Track BBJ time and 400m split separately each round.  
**Scaling:** Reduce BBJ to 12 m (beginner). Advanced: 20 m per round + 600 m runs.

---

### HIIT #7 — Farmers Carry + Lunges Superset (Phase 2)
**Format:** 4 Rounds, Every 5:00  
**Duration:** 20 minutes  
**Target:** Grip endurance, lunge efficiency, postural integrity under load

| Round | Movement A | Movement B | Prescription |
|-------|-----------|-----------|-------------|
| Each round | Farmers Carry | 100 m @ 2×24 kg | Fast walk, 0 planned stops |
| Then | Sandbag Lunges | 25 m @ 20 kg | 0.9–1.0 m steps, touch-and-go |

**Rest:** Remaining time in the 5:00 window. Target: complete both movements in 2:30–3:30, leaving 1:30–2:30 rest.  
**Intensity:** RPE 7. Focus on grip management — chalk hands before round 1.  
**Scaling:** 2×16 kg carries + 10 kg sandbag (beginner). Advanced: 2×32 kg + 30 kg sandbag.

---

### HIIT #8 — The Grinder: BBJ + Wall Ball + Lunge Chipper (Phase 2)
**Format:** For Time (Chipper)  
**Duration:** 25–35 minutes (time cap: 38 min)  
**Target:** Full-body Hyrox station stamina; pacing across multiple fatiguing stations

| Order | Movement | Prescription |
|-------|----------|-------------|
| 1 | Burpee Broad Jumps | 60 m |
| 2 | Wall Balls | 75 reps @ 6 kg to 10 ft |
| 3 | Sandbag Lunges | 75 m @ 20 kg |
| 4 | Wall Balls | 25 reps @ 6 kg |
| 5 | Burpee Broad Jumps | 20 m |

**Rest:** Self-regulated. Planned micro-breaks only (3–5 sec).  
**Intensity:** RPE 8. Wall ball break strategy: 25-25-25 on the first set of 75. Lunges: continuous.  
**Target time:** Sub-30 min.  
**Scaling:** Reduce BBJ to 40 m + 50 WB + 50 m lunges + 15 WB + 10 m BBJ. Advanced: all distances/reps at full race spec + add 200 m run between each movement.

---

### HIIT #9 — SkiErg + Sled Pull EMOM (Phase 2)
**Format:** EMOM 20  
**Duration:** 20 minutes  
**Target:** Upper body pulling endurance, aerobic capacity

| Minute | Movement | Prescription |
|--------|----------|-------------|
| Min 1 | SkiErg | 18 cal |
| Min 2 | Sled Pull | 1 × 12.5 m @ 90% race weight |
| Min 3 | SkiErg | 18 cal |
| Min 4 | Rest | Active: walk, shake arms |
| Repeat 5 rounds |||

**Intensity:** RPE 7. SkiErg split: 1:50–2:00/500m. Sled pull: complete in <30 sec per 12.5m.  
**Scaling:** 14 cal SkiErg, 80% sled weight (beginner). Advanced: 22 cal SkiErg, 100% sled weight, remove rest minute (EMOM 15: 3 movements per 5-min block).

---

### HIIT #10 — Compromised Running Circuit (Phase 2)
**Format:** 4 Rounds For Time  
**Duration:** 30–40 minutes (time cap: 42 min)  
**Target:** Running under fatigue — the defining Hyrox skill

| Round | Segment | Prescription |
|-------|---------|-------------|
| A | Sled Push | 50 m @ 90% race weight |
| B | Run | 1 km @ goal Hyrox pace |
| C | Row | 500 m @ 1:55–2:05/500m |
| D | Run | 1 km @ goal Hyrox pace |

**Rest:** None between segments. 60 sec between rounds (walk, sip water).  
**Intensity:** RPE 8. The runs are the focus — track every 1 km split.  
**Target time:** 32–36 min. Run splits should be within 10 sec of each other.  
**Scaling:** Remove 1 round (3 rounds total) or reduce sled to 80% and row to 400m. Advanced: add BBJ 20m after the sled push.

---

### HIIT #11 — Tabata Station Blitz (Phase 2/3)
**Format:** Tabata (20 sec on / 10 sec off × 8 rounds per station, 1 min between stations)  
**Duration:** 24 minutes  
**Target:** Anaerobic capacity across multiple movement patterns

| Station (4 min each) | Movement | Prescription |
|----------------------|----------|-------------|
| Station A | Wall Balls | 20 sec max reps @ 6 kg → 10 sec rest × 8 rounds |
| 1 min rest |||
| Station B | Burpee Broad Jump | 20 sec max distance → 10 sec rest × 8 |
| 1 min rest |||
| Station C | SkiErg | 20 sec max cal → 10 sec rest × 8 |
| 1 min rest |||
| Station D | Sandbag Lunges | 20 sec max distance @ 20 kg → 10 sec rest × 8 |

**Score:** Total reps (WB), total distance (BBJ + lunges), total calories (SkiErg).  
**Intensity:** RPE 9–10 during work intervals. Full send.  
**Scaling:** 4 kg wall ball, no sandbag on lunges (beginner). Advanced: 9 kg wall ball, 30 kg sandbag.

---

### HIIT #12 — Race Pace Station Intervals (Phase 3)
**Format:** Every 4:00 × 8 Sets  
**Duration:** 32 minutes  
**Target:** Each station practiced at race-weight, race-pace conditions with timed recovery

| Set | Station | Prescription | Target Time |
|-----|---------|-------------|-------------|
| 1 | SkiErg 500 m | Race pace: 1:50–1:55/500m | ~1:55 |
| 2 | Sled Push 50 m | 100% race weight (152 kg) | <3:00 |
| 3 | Sled Pull 50 m | 100% race weight (103 kg) | <3:30 |
| 4 | BBJ 40 m | Step-up, consistent tempo | <2:30 |
| 5 | Row 500 m | Race pace: 1:50–1:55/500m | ~1:55 |
| 6 | Farmers Carry 100 m | 2×24 kg, fast walk | <1:15 |
| 7 | Sandbag Lunges 50 m | 20 kg, 0.9 m steps | <2:30 |
| 8 | Wall Balls 50 reps | 6 kg to 10 ft, sets of 25 | <3:00 |

**Rest:** Remaining time in the 4:00 window.  
**Intensity:** RPE 7–8. The goal is consistency and pacing, not redlining.  
**Scoring:** Sum of all 8 station times. Compare week-over-week.  
**Scaling:** 50% distances/reps per station (beginner). Advanced: 4-min windows → 3:30 windows.

---

### HIIT #13 — Wall Ball Century (Phase 3)
**Format:** For Time  
**Duration:** 8–14 minutes  
**Target:** Full 100-rep wall ball performance with race-day break strategy

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Set 1 | 25 Wall Balls @ 6 kg to 10 ft |
| Rest | 5 sec (ball down, shake arms, 3 breaths) |
| Set 2 | 25 Wall Balls |
| Rest | 5 sec |
| Set 3 | 25 Wall Balls |
| Rest | 5 sec |
| Set 4 | 25 Wall Balls |

**Intensity:** RPE 8–9. Cadence: one rep every 3 sec. Total target: 5:30–6:30.  
**Key coaching cue:** If any set takes >100 sec, you started too fast. The 4×25 pattern trains the exact break strategy to use on race day.  
**Scaling:** 4×15 (60 total, beginner). Advanced: 50-25-25 or unbroken attempt.

---

### HIIT #14 — 4-Station Hyrox Block (Phase 3)
**Format:** For Time  
**Duration:** 35–50 minutes (time cap: 55 min)  
**Target:** Race-specific block simulation — Stations 5–8 + corresponding runs

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Row | 1,000 m @ 1:52–1:58/500m |
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Farmers Carry | 200 m @ 2×24 kg |
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Sandbag Lunges | 100 m @ 20 kg |
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Wall Balls | 100 reps @ 6 kg to 10 ft |

**Rest:** None. Treat Roxzone transitions as race-pace jogs (target <45 sec per transition).  
**Intensity:** RPE 8. This is race-simulation intensity for the second half.  
**Target time:** 38–45 min (4 km running + 4 stations).  
**Scoring:** Total time. Also record: each 1 km run split, each station time, each transition time. Compare to race-day targets.

---

### HIIT #15 — Sled + Row Superset (Phase 3)
**Format:** 5 Rounds, Every 5:00  
**Duration:** 25 minutes  
**Target:** Sled push at race weight + rowing recovery pacing

| Round | Movement A | Movement B |
|-------|-----------|-----------|
| Each round | Sled Push: 50 m @ 152 kg (race weight) | Row: 250 m @ 1:55–2:00/500m |

**Rest:** Remaining time in 5:00 window. Target: sled in ~2:30–3:00, row in ~55 sec. Total work ~3:30–4:00, rest ~60–90 sec.  
**Intensity:** RPE 8. Focus on sled technique: 45° angle, short steps, never stop.  
**Scaling:** 122 kg sled + 200 m row (beginner). Advanced: 170 kg sled (overload) + 300 m row.

---

### HIIT #16 — Stations 1–4 Block Simulation (Phase 3)
**Format:** For Time  
**Duration:** 30–42 minutes (time cap: 45 min)  
**Target:** Race-specific first-half simulation

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| SkiErg | 1,000 m |
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Sled Push | 50 m @ 152 kg |
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Sled Pull | 50 m @ 103 kg |
| Run | 1 km @ goal pace |
| Burpee Broad Jump | 80 m |

**Rest:** None. Jog transitions.  
**Intensity:** RPE 8. Conservative on Run 1 — build across runs.  
**Target time:** 32–40 min. First km: 4:40–4:50. Final km: 4:50–5:00 (allow 10 sec drift).

---

### HIIT #17 — Taper Sharpener EMOM (Phase 4)
**Format:** EMOM 15  
**Duration:** 15 minutes  
**Target:** Race-weight touchpoints at reduced volume; neural activation, not fatigue

| Minute | Movement | Prescription |
|--------|----------|-------------|
| Min 1 | SkiErg | 12 cal |
| Min 2 | Wall Balls | 10 reps @ 6 kg |
| Min 3 | Row | 12 cal |
| Min 4 | Sandbag Lunges | 15 m @ 20 kg |
| Min 5 | Rest | Walk, shake out |
| Repeat 3 rounds |||

**Intensity:** RPE 6–7. This should feel "comfortable-hard" — practiced, controlled, smooth.  
**Scaling:** Not applicable — this is already reduced volume. Advanced athletes may increase to 15 cal / 15 reps / 20 m.

---

### HIIT #18 — AMRAP 20: Hyrox Engine Test (Phase 2/3)
**Format:** 20-Minute AMRAP  
**Duration:** 20 minutes  
**Target:** Sustained mixed-modal output; benchmarking tool

| Movement | Prescription |
|----------|-------------|
| Row | 250 m |
| Wall Balls | 15 reps @ 6 kg |
| Burpee Broad Jump | 10 m |
| Sandbag Lunges | 15 m @ 20 kg |
| SkiErg | 250 m |

**Score:** Completed rounds + reps. Repeat at Weeks 6 and 11 to track progress.  
**Intensity:** RPE 8. Pacing is everything — start conservatively, aim for consistent round times.  
**Target:** 4–6 rounds for intermediate; 6–8 for advanced.  
**Scaling:** Remove SkiErg or row per round (4 movements instead of 5). Advanced: increase to 300 m erg distances.

---

### HIIT #19 — Race-Pace Express (Phase 4)
**Format:** For Time  
**Duration:** 15–22 minutes (time cap: 25 min)  
**Target:** Race-day rehearsal at half volume

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Run | 1 km @ race pace |
| Sled Push | 25 m @ 152 kg (half distance) |
| Run | 1 km @ race pace |
| Wall Balls | 50 reps @ 6 kg |

**Rest:** None. Practice Roxzone transitions.  
**Intensity:** RPE 7. Should feel "race sharp" not exhausting.  
**Target time:** 16–20 min. Use this to confirm race-day pacing targets.

---

### HIIT #20 — Race Primer EMOM (Race Week — Phase 4)
**Format:** EMOM 10  
**Duration:** 10 minutes  
**Target:** Race-weight neural activation 4–5 days before race

| Minute | Movement | Prescription |
|--------|----------|-------------|
| Min 1 | SkiErg | 10 cal |
| Min 2 | Wall Balls | 8 reps @ 6 kg |
| Min 3 | Row | 10 cal |
| Min 4 | Farmers Carry | 30 m @ 2×24 kg |
| Min 5 | BBJ | 8 m |
| Min 6 | Sandbag Lunges | 10 m @ 20 kg |
| Min 7 | SkiErg | 10 cal |
| Min 8 | Wall Balls | 8 reps |
| Min 9 | Row | 10 cal |
| Min 10 | Easy Walk | Cooldown |

**Intensity:** RPE 5–6. Light, smooth, rehearsal-quality. This is NOT a training stimulus — it is a neural primer.

## 4. Hyrox Simulation Workouts

### Simulation #1 — Baseline Benchmark (Week 4 Deload)
**Format:** Partial Simulation — 4 stations + 4 km running  
**When:** Saturday of Week 4  
**Duration:** 35–50 min  
**Purpose:** Establish baseline times for all stations and running

| Segment | Prescription | Record |
|---------|-------------|--------|
| Run 1 | 1 km | Split time |
| SkiErg | 1,000 m | Station time |
| Run 2 | 1 km | Split time |
| Sled Push | 50 m @ 100% race weight (152 kg) | Station time |
| Run 3 | 1 km | Split time |
| Row | 1,000 m | Station time |
| Run 4 | 1 km | Split time |
| Wall Balls | 100 reps @ 6 kg to 10 ft | Station time |

**Notes:** Record total time AND individual segment times. This is your benchmark against which all future progress is measured. Pace runs at goal race pace. Go 85% effort on stations — save 100% for the actual race.

---

### Simulation #2 — Half-Simulation (Week 8 Deload)
**Format:** Stations 1–4 + 4 km running (first half of race)  
**When:** Saturday of Week 8  
**Duration:** 30–42 min

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Run 1 → SkiErg 1,000 m → Run 2 → Sled Push 50 m @ 152 kg → Run 3 → Sled Pull 50 m @ 103 kg → Run 4 → BBJ 80 m |

**Purpose:** Test first-half race execution. Track all splits. Compare Run 1 vs. Run 4 pace degradation (target: <15 sec/km drift). Compare station times to Week 4 benchmark.

---

### Simulation #3 — Full Simulation (Week 10)
**Format:** Full 8-station Hyrox simulation  
**When:** Saturday of Week 10  
**Duration:** 65–85 min  
**Purpose:** Complete race dress rehearsal. This is the highest-volume simulation of the entire plan.

| Segment | Prescription | Target Time |
|---------|-------------|-------------|
| Run 1 (1 km) | @ 4:40/km | 4:40 |
| SkiErg 1,000 m | @ 1:55/500m | 3:50 |
| Run 2 (1 km) | @ 4:40/km | 4:40 |
| Sled Push 50 m | @ 152 kg, continuous | 2:50 |
| Run 3 (1 km) | @ 4:45/km | 4:45 |
| Sled Pull 50 m | @ 103 kg | 3:30 |
| Run 4 (1 km) | @ 4:45/km | 4:45 |
| BBJ 80 m | Step-up, steady | 3:30 |
| Run 5 (1 km) | @ 4:50/km | 4:50 |
| Row 1,000 m | @ 1:55/500m | 3:50 |
| Run 6 (1 km) | @ 4:50/km | 4:50 |
| Farmers Carry 200 m | @ 2×24 kg | 1:45 |
| Run 7 (1 km) | @ 4:50/km | 4:50 |
| Sandbag Lunges 100 m | @ 20 kg | 4:30 |
| Run 8 (1 km) | @ 4:55/km | 4:55 |
| Wall Balls 100 reps | @ 6 kg, 4×25 | 5:30 |

**Total target: ~68–72 min.** Record everything. This is your predicted race time ± 3–5 min (race-day adrenaline and fresh legs may improve by 3–5%).

**Nutrition practice:** Use race-day nutrition during this simulation — test gels, electrolytes, timing. Take a gel between Station 4 (BBJ) and Run 5.

---

### Simulation #4 — Three-Quarter Simulation (Week 12 Deload)
**Format:** Stations 4–8 + 5 runs (second half emphasis)  
**When:** Saturday of Week 12  
**Duration:** 40–55 min

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Run → BBJ 80 m → Run → Row 1,000 m → Run → Farmers Carry 200 m → Run → Sandbag Lunges 100 m → Run → Wall Balls 100 reps |

**Purpose:** The second half of the race is where most time is lost. This simulation specifically trains the lunge → wall ball connection (r = 0.738 correlation per HyroxDataLab) and late-race running under deep fatigue.

---

### Simulation #5 — Dress Rehearsal: Half-Simulation (Week 14)
**Format:** Abbreviated race rehearsal — 4 stations, 4 km, reduced intensity  
**When:** Thursday of Week 14  
**Duration:** 30–40 min

| Segment | Prescription |
|---------|-------------|
| Run 1 km → SkiErg 750 m → Run 1 km → Sled Push 25 m @ 152 kg → Run 1 km → Wall Balls 50 reps → Run 1 km |

**Purpose:** Final confidence-builder. Reduced volume but full race weight. Practice pacing, transitions, nutrition timing, and mental routine. Should feel EASY — RPE 6–7 max. If it doesn't feel easy, the taper is working.

---

### Simulation Deployment Schedule Summary

| Week | Simulation | Type | Volume | Intensity |
|------|-----------|------|--------|-----------|
| 4 | #1 Baseline Benchmark | Partial (4 stations) | Moderate | 85% |
| 8 | #2 Half-Simulation | First-half race | High | 90% |
| 10 | #3 Full Simulation | Complete race | Maximum | 90–95% |
| 12 | #4 Three-Quarter Sim | Second-half race | High | 88% |
| 14 | #5 Dress Rehearsal | Abbreviated half | Low-moderate | 70–75% |

---

## 5. Progressive Overload Strategy

### 5.1 Running Progression

| Variable | Phase 1 (Wk 1–4) | Phase 2 (Wk 5–8) | Phase 3 (Wk 9–12) | Phase 4 (Wk 13–16) |
|----------|------------------|------------------|-------------------|---------------------|
| Weekly mileage | 35–38 mi | 36–40 mi | 35–38 mi | 28–15 mi (↓) |
| Long run distance | 10 mi | 11 mi | 10 mi | 8 → 6 → 0 mi |
| Tempo run distance | 3 mi @ threshold | 3–4 mi @ threshold | 4 mi @ race pace | 2 mi @ race pace |
| VO₂max intervals | 4×4 min | 4×4 min | 5×4 min or 6×3 min | 3×4 min → 0 |
| Compromised runs | 0 | 1/week (2.5 mi post-strength) | 2/week (within HIIT sessions) | 1/week (within reduced HIIT) |
| Easy run pace | 8:00–8:30/mi | 8:00–8:30/mi | 8:00–8:30/mi | 8:00–8:30/mi |
| Goal race pace target | 7:15–7:30/mi (4:30–4:40/km) | 7:05–7:20/mi (4:25–4:35/km) | 7:00–7:15/mi (4:20–4:30/km) | Maintain Phase 3 pace |

**Progression logic:** Mileage builds 5–8% per 3-week block then drops 20–25% on deload week. Intensity (tempo/interval pace) improves as aerobic base adapts. Compromised running is added in Phase 2 and increased in Phase 3 because the ability to run well under station fatigue is the single most trainable Hyrox limiter.

### 5.2 Station-Specific Progression

| Station | Phase 1 Load/Volume | Phase 2 | Phase 3 | Phase 4 |
|---------|-------------------|---------|---------|---------|
| **Sled Push** | 122 kg (80%), 2×50m per session | 137 kg (90%), 4×50m | 152 kg (100%), 4×50m | 152 kg, 2×50m (reduced vol) |
| **Sled Pull** | 82 kg (80%), 2×50m | 93 kg (90%), 4×50m | 103 kg (100%), 4×50m | 103 kg, 2×50m |
| **Wall Balls** | 6 kg, sets of 15–25, total 75/session | 6 kg, sets of 25, total 100/session | 6 kg, 4×25 or unbroken 100 | 6 kg, 50 reps max |
| **BBJ** | 20–40 m per session | 40–60 m | 80 m (full race distance) | 40 m |
| **Lunges** | 20 kg, 25–50 m per session | 20 kg, 50–75 m | 20 kg, 100 m (full race distance) | 20 kg, 50 m |
| **Farmers Carry** | 2×24 kg, 50–100 m | 2×24 kg, 100–150 m | 2×24 kg, 200 m (full race distance) | 2×24 kg, 100 m |
| **SkiErg** | 500 m intervals | 750 m intervals | 1,000 m (full race distance) | 500 m (maintenance) |
| **Row** | 500 m intervals | 750 m intervals | 1,000 m (full race distance) | 500 m |

**Progression logic:** Load increases linearly from 80% → 90% → 100% race weight across Phases 1–3. Volume increases alongside load (more sets, longer distances) until Phase 3 reaches full race specifications. Phase 4 maintains race-weight loads but cuts volume by ~50% to preserve freshness.

### 5.3 Strength Progression

| Phase | Squat Protocol | Deadlift Protocol | Accessory Focus | Sessions/Week |
|-------|---------------|-------------------|-----------------|---------------|
| Phase 1 | Back Squat 4×5 @ 80% → 4×4 @ 83% → 4×3 @ 85% | Deadlift 3×5 @ 78% → 3×4 @ 82% | Pull-ups, rows, RDL, walking lunges | 2 |
| Phase 2 | Front Squat 3×8 @ 72% → 3×6 @ 75% | RDL 3×8 @ 70% | DB lunges, GHD, farmer holds | 2 |
| Phase 3 | Back Squat 3×4 @ 82% (maintenance) | Deadlift 3×3 @ 85% (maintenance) | Single-leg work, core stability | 1–2 |
| Phase 4 | Back Squat 2×4 @ 78% (activation) | Deadlift 2×3 @ 75% (light) | Minimal — pull-ups 2×8, plank 2×45s | 1 |

**Progression logic:** Phase 1 follows classic 5-3-1 progression building toward high relative intensity. Phase 2 shifts to hypertrophy/strength-endurance rep ranges (6–10 reps) to support station demands. Phase 3 reverts to low-rep, moderate-load maintenance — the goal is to preserve strength without accumulating fatigue. Phase 4 is activation only.

### 5.4 HIIT Complexity & Density Progression

| Variable | Phase 1 | Phase 2 | Phase 3 | Phase 4 |
|----------|---------|---------|---------|---------|
| Sessions/week | 2 | 3 | 3 | 2 → 1 |
| Avg session duration | 35–45 min | 45–55 min | 50–65 min | 30–40 min |
| Time domains | 10–20 min pieces | 15–25 min pieces | 20–40 min pieces | 10–15 min pieces |
| Work:rest ratios | 1:1 to 1:2 | 1:0.75 to 1:1 | 1:0.5 to 1:1 | 1:1 to 1:2 |
| Station load | 80% race weight | 90% race weight | 100% race weight | 100% load, 50% volume |
| Movements per session | 2–4 stations | 3–6 stations | 4–8 stations (full race) | 2–4 stations |
| Compromised running included | No | Yes (1/session) | Yes (2–4 km per session) | Yes (1–2 km) |

---

## 6. Taper Protocol

### 6.1 Final 14-Day Taper Strategy (Weeks 15–16)

The taper follows the evidence-based model: **reduce volume 40–60%** while **maintaining or slightly increasing intensity** on key sessions. This preserves neuromuscular readiness and aerobic fitness while allowing full glycogen resynthesis, muscle repair, and psychological freshness.

| Day (countdown) | Date | Session | Volume vs. Peak | Intensity | Notes |
|-----------------|------|---------|----------------|-----------|-------|
| Day -14 | May 23 (Fri) | Easy Run 5 mi | 60% | Zone 2 | Last "normal" easy run |
| Day -13 | May 24 (Sat) | HIIT #17 (Taper Sharpener) | 50% | RPE 7 | Reduced-volume EMOM, race-weight touch |
| Day -12 | May 25 (Sun) | Rest | 0% | — | Full rest |
| Day -11 | May 26 (Mon) | Easy Run 5 mi + Strides | 55% | Zone 2 + 4×100m strides | Neuromuscular activation |
| Day -10 | May 27 (Tue) | Strength (Light) 40 min | 40% | RPE 5–6 | 2×4 squat @ 78%, 2×6 RDL, 2×8 pull-ups |
| Day -9 | May 28 (Wed) | Interval Run (Reduced) | 50% | 3×4 min @ 90% HRmax | Last real VO₂max session |
| Day -8 | May 29 (Thu) | Rest or 20 min walk | 0% | — | Mental prep begins |
| Day -7 | May 30 (Fri) | Easy Run 4 mi | 40% | Zone 2 | Gentle shakeout |
| Day -6 | May 31 (Sat) | HIIT #20 (Race Primer EMOM) 10 min | 25% | RPE 5–6 | Neural priming only — race-weight stations at 50% volume |
| Day -5 | Jun 1 (Sun) | Rest | 0% | — | Full rest |
| Day -4 | Jun 2 (Mon) | Easy Run 3 mi + 4×80m strides | 30% | Zone 2 + strides at mile pace | Last real workout |
| Day -3 | Jun 3 (Tue) | Rest / 15-min walk | 0% | — | Optional light walk |
| Day -2 | Jun 4 (Wed) | Shakeout 2 mi + 2×30-sec pickups | 20% | Easy + 2 race-pace bursts | Neural priming, confidence builder |
| Day -1 | Jun 5 (Thu) | Rest | 0% | — | Gear prep, hydrate, carb-load, visualize |
| **Race Day** | Jun 6 (Fri) | **HYROX** | 100% | Race effort | Execute the plan |

### 6.2 What to Cut vs. Maintain

| Cut | Maintain |
|-----|---------|
| Running volume (down 40–60%) | Running intensity on 1–2 key sessions (strides, race-pace pickups) |
| HIIT session count (3/wk → 1 → 0) | Race-weight station touchpoints (short, low-volume) |
| Strength sessions (2/wk → 1 → 0) | Mobility and foam rolling (daily) |
| Long run (eliminated by Week 15) | Sleep quality (8+ hours/night, strict) |
| Session duration (drop from 60 min → 30 min → 20 min) | Nutrition quality and carb-loading protocol |
| All high-volume conditioning | Short-burst neuromuscular activation (strides, pickups) |

### 6.3 Race Day Warm-Up Protocol

**Timing:** Begin 40 minutes before wave start. Arrive at venue 70–90 minutes before start.

| Phase | Time Before Start | Duration | Activity |
|-------|------------------|----------|----------|
| 1: Aerobic Activation | T-40 min | 8 min | Light jog around venue or on BikeErg (Zone 1–2, easy) |
| 2: Dynamic Mobility | T-32 min | 5 min | Leg swings (front/back, lateral), hip circles, arm circles, ankle rolls, thoracic rotation |
| 3: Intensity Ramp | T-27 min | 8 min | 500 m SkiErg @ race pace (1:55/500m), 400 m run at goal race pace, 5 wall balls @ race weight, 3 BBJ |
| 4: Race-Pace Strides | T-19 min | 5 min | 4×100 m strides at race pace with walk-back recovery |
| 5: Station Priming | T-14 min | 4 min | If sled available: 1×12.5 m push at race weight. If not: 10 bodyweight squats, 10 push-ups, 5 broad jumps |
| 6: Mental Reset | T-10 min | 5 min | Deep breathing (4-count in, 4-hold, 6-out). Visualize first 3 stations. Review pacing targets on wrist/arm. Find your mantra. |
| 7: Assembly | T-5 min | — | Enter Start Zone. Put on timing chip. Confirm wave number matches arm marking. Controlled breathing. |

**Race-Day Pacing Targets to Write on Arm:**

| Segment | Target Time |
|---------|-------------|
| Run 1 | 4:40 (conservative start) |
| SkiErg | 3:50 |
| Run 2 | 4:35 |
| Sled Push | 2:50 |
| Run 3 | 4:40 |
| Sled Pull | 3:30 |
| Run 4 | 4:45 |
| BBJ | 3:30 |
| Run 5 | 4:50 |
| Row | 3:50 |
| Run 6 | 4:50 |
| Farmers | 1:40 |
| Run 7 | 4:50 |
| Lunges | 4:30 |
| Run 8 | 4:55 |
| Wall Balls | 5:30 |
| **Total Target** | **~67–72 min** |

# HYROX Complete Reference Document — AI Coach Knowledge Base

> **Sources cited throughout:** Official HYROX 25/26 Season Rulebook (hyrox.com), roxlyfe.com, hyroxdatalab.com, hybridfitnessmedia.com, pace-club.com, Brandt et al. (2025) published in *Frontiers in Physiology*, Men's Health UK, Concept2.com, fitnessexperiment.co, warriorperformancelab.com.

---

## 1. HYROX Event Format — Complete Reference

### 1.1 Core Concept

HYROX is an indoor mass-participation fitness race combining running and functional workout stations. It was co-founded by Christian Toetzke and designed by Mintra Tilly (Director of Sport). The format is standardised worldwide: **8 × 1 km runs** alternating with **8 functional workout stations**, always performed in the same fixed order. Every racer — regardless of division — runs the same total distance of **8 km**. Divisions differ only in the weights, loads, and (historically) rep counts at the stations.

*(Source: Official HYROX 25/26 Singles Rulebook, Section 1 "Concept")*

### 1.2 Station Order and Race Sequence

The race always follows this exact sequence:

| Segment | Activity |
|---------|----------|
| Run 1 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 1** | SkiErg — 1,000 m |
| Run 2 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 2** | Sled Push — 50 m (4 × 12.5 m) |
| Run 3 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 3** | Sled Pull — 50 m (4 × 12.5 m) |
| Run 4 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 4** | Burpee Broad Jump — 80 m |
| Run 5 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 5** | Rowing — 1,000 m |
| Run 6 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 6** | Farmers Carry — 200 m |
| Run 7 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 7** | Sandbag Lunges — 100 m |
| Run 8 (1 km) | → |
| **Station 8** | Wall Balls — 100 reps |
| **→ Finish Line** | |

*(Source: Official HYROX 25/26 Singles Rulebook, Section 4.1)*

### 1.3 Complete Station Weights, Distances, and Reps by Division

The following table contains the **exact** specifications from the official 2025/26 HYROX Rulebook. Note that Women's Pro and Men's Open share identical weights across all stations.

| Station | Distance / Reps | Women's Open | Women's Pro | Men's Open | Men's Pro |
|---------|----------------|-------------|------------|-----------|----------|
| **1. SkiErg** | 1,000 m | 1,000 m | 1,000 m | 1,000 m | 1,000 m |
| **2. Sled Push** | 4 × 12.5 m (50 m) | **102 kg** incl. sled (~50 kg added) | **152 kg** incl. sled (~100 kg added) | **152 kg** incl. sled (~100 kg added) | **202 kg** incl. sled (~150 kg added) |
| **3. Sled Pull** | 4 × 12.5 m (50 m) | **78 kg** incl. sled (~25 kg added) | **103 kg** incl. sled (~50 kg added) | **103 kg** incl. sled (~50 kg added) | **153 kg** incl. sled (~100 kg added) |
| **4. Burpee Broad Jump** | 80 m | 80 m | 80 m | 80 m | 80 m |
| **5. Rowing** | 1,000 m | 1,000 m | 1,000 m | 1,000 m | 1,000 m |
| **6. Farmers Carry** | 200 m | **2 × 16 kg** (white) | **2 × 24 kg** (grey) | **2 × 24 kg** (grey) | **2 × 32 kg** (black) |
| **7. Sandbag Lunges** | 100 m | **10 kg** (white) | **20 kg** (grey) | **20 kg** (grey) | **30 kg** (black) |
| **8. Wall Balls** | 100 reps | **4 kg / 9 lbs** (white) | **6 kg / 14 lbs** (grey) | **6 kg / 14 lbs** (grey) | **9 kg / 20 lbs** (black) |
| Wall Ball Target Height | — | **2.70 m** (9 ft) | **2.70 m** (9 ft) | **3.00 m** (10 ft) | **3.00 m** (10 ft) |

*(Source: Official HYROX 25/26 Singles Rulebook, Section 4.1 and Sections 9.1–9.8; confirmed by pace-club.com and roxlyfe.com)*

**Key note:** At the World Championships, all individual qualifiers in age groups U24–59 (regardless of whether they qualified in Open) must race with **Pro weights**. Only athletes aged 60+ retain Open weights at Worlds.

### 1.4 Equipment Specifications

| Equipment | Brand/Model | Details |
|-----------|------------|---------|
| **SkiErg** | Concept2 SkiErg (with floor stand) | Damper preset to **Resistance 6** (racer may adjust). Weight ~21 kg (machine) + 16 kg (floor stand). |
| **Rowing Machine** | Concept2 RowErg (standard model) | Damper preset to **Resistance 6** (racer may adjust). Foot plates preset to **Position 4** (racer may adjust). Length 244 cm, weight 26 kg. |
| **Sleds** | HYROX-branded competition sleds | Sled base weight is approximately 52 kg (varies slightly). All stated weights are **inclusive of sled**. Lanes are 12.5 m long. Sled pull uses a rope. |
| **Kettlebells** | Competition kettlebells | Colour-coded: White = 16 kg, Grey = 24 kg, Black = 32 kg. |
| **Sandbags** | HYROX-branded sandbags | Colour-coded: White = 10 kg, Grey = 20 kg, Black = 30 kg. Carried on both shoulders. |
| **Wall Balls** | Medicine balls / Wall balls | Colour-coded: White = 4 kg (9 lbs), Grey = 6 kg (14 lbs), Black = 9 kg (20 lbs). Targets are mounted on a purpose-built wall ball rig. Some venues now use **digital wall ball targets** that auto-count reps. |
| **Warm-Up Area** | Concept2 BikeErg available | Plus other equipment for pre-race preparation. |

*(Sources: Concept2.com/hyrox, Official HYROX Rulebook 25/26, pace-club.com)*

### 1.5 Course Layout

HYROX events are held in **large indoor venues** (convention centres, exhibition halls, arenas). The course layout follows a consistent template across all global events:

- **Running Track:** An approximately 1 km loop laid out **around the perimeter** (outside edge) of the venue. Depending on venue size, each 1 km run may consist of 1–5 laps. A dividing line splits the track into a **Fast Lane** (inside, for racers at ≤4:00/km pace) and a **Running Lane** (outside, for all others).
- **Roxzone (Transition Zone):** The central area **inside** the running track. Athletes enter and exit the Roxzone through clearly marked **IN and OUT arches** along one side of the running track. The Roxzone typically adds approximately **800 m to 1 km** of additional movement distance across the full race (jogging/walking between the running track and the workout stations).
- **Workout Stations:** All 8 stations are set up **inside** the Roxzone, in the centre of the venue. They are arranged sequentially so athletes proceed through them in order.
- **Start Tunnel:** A designated tunnel/chute where athletes assemble before their wave start.
- **Finish Line:** Positioned after the Wall Ball station (Station 8). Athletes proceed from Wall Balls to a "Finisher Stage" and cross the finish line.
- **Spectator Areas:** Marked zones adjacent to the Roxzone where spectators can watch the workout stations.

*(Sources: Official HYROX Rulebook, fitnessexperiment.co course layout analysis, rox-coach.com Roxzone guide)*

### 1.6 Wave Start System and Timing

HYROX uses a **wave start system** with waves departing at regular intervals, typically **every 10 minutes**. Key timing details:

- Each racer is assigned a specific start time communicated before race day and confirmed at check-in.
- The start time must be **written visibly on the racer's arm**.
- Starting in any wave other than the assigned one (without prior approval) results in **disqualification**.
- Racers within the same wave are always from the **same division** (e.g., all Men's Pro start together).
- A **timing chip** worn on the ankle records splits for each run, each Roxzone entry/exit, and each station completion. Doubles teams carry 2 chips; Relay teams carry 4.
- Racers must assemble in the **Start Zone Area** 10 minutes before their wave time.
- Wristband colour indicates division: White (Women's Open), Grey (Women's Pro / Men's Open), Black (Men's Pro), and/or Green (for specific identifiers).

*(Source: Official HYROX 25/26 Rulebook, Sections 8 and 12)*

### 1.7 Transition Zone (Roxzone) Rules and Penalties

| Rule | Detail | Penalty |
|------|--------|---------|
| Enter Roxzone via **IN arch** | Must use correct arch when coming off the running track | **2 min penalty** per infringement for using OUT arch to enter |
| Exit Roxzone via **OUT arch** | Must use correct arch when returning to running track | **2 min penalty** per infringement for using IN arch to exit |
| No outside assistance | No food, drink, or help from spectators/coaches in Roxzone | **3 min penalty** per infringement (classified as outside assistance) |
| Water provided at aid stations only | Fluids available at designated aid stations within Roxzone | Water is for **drinking only** — not for active cooling (pouring over body). 2 min penalty. |
| No littering | Paper cups and gel wrappers must be placed in bins | **2 min penalty** per infringement |
| No spitting / nose clearing on floor | Hygiene rule | **2 min penalty** per infringement |
| Chalk usage | Only event-provided chalk may be used, and **only at Sled Pull and Farmers Carry** | **2 min penalty** for using chalk at any other station |
| Shoes | Must be worn at all times except at Wall Balls, where they may be removed and placed under the rig. Must be carried to finisher stage after Wall Balls. | — |

*(Source: Official HYROX 25/26 Rulebook, Sections 8.1, 11, 13)*

### 1.8 Doubles Format Differences

HYROX Doubles is a **two-person team** format available in the following divisions:
- **Men's Doubles** (Open or Pro)
- **Women's Doubles** (Open or Pro)
- **Mixed Doubles** (Open only at regular events)

Key differences from Singles:

| Aspect | Singles | Doubles |
|--------|---------|---------|
| Running | Individual runs all 8 km | **Both partners run together** for all 8 × 1 km. Must stay together (penalty for separation: 1 min per run/station, DQ after 3rd infringement). |
| Stations | Individual completes every station | Partners **split each station** however they choose (e.g., one does 60 wall balls, the other does 40). Only one partner works at a time; the other waits. |
| Sled distances | 4 × 12.5 m | **8 × 12.5 m** (doubled distance for most stations) |
| Burpee Broad Jump | 80 m | **160 m total** (split between partners) |
| Farmers Carry | 200 m | **400 m total** (split between partners) |
| Sandbag Lunges | 100 m | **200 m total** (split between partners) |
| SkiErg | 1,000 m | **2,000 m total** |
| Rowing | 1,000 m | **2,000 m total** |
| Wall Balls | 100 reps | **200 reps total** |
| Weights (Open) | As per Open singles table | Same Open weights |
| Weights (Pro) | As per Pro singles table | Same Pro weights |
| Mixed Doubles | N/A | Uses **Men's Open weights** for all stations (which equals Women's Pro weights). Women's target height (2.70 m) for wall balls. |

*(Sources: Official HYROX 25/26 Doubles Rulebook, warriorperformancelab.com, fitnessexperiment.co)*

### 1.9 Relay Format

The **Team Relay** is a 4-person event. Each team member completes **2 running segments and 2 workout stations**:
- Person 1: Run 1 → SkiErg → Run 2 → Sled Push
- Person 2: Run 3 → Sled Pull → Run 4 → Burpee Broad Jump
- Person 3: Run 5 → Rowing → Run 6 → Farmers Carry
- Person 4: Run 7 → Sandbag Lunges → Run 8 → Wall Balls

Available as Men's Relay, Women's Relay, and Mixed Relay. Uses Open weights.

### 1.10 Recent Rule Changes for the 2025/26 Season

| Change | Detail | Effective |
|--------|--------|-----------|
| **Women's Open Wall Balls: 75 → 100 reps** | Women's Open and Women's Open Doubles now do **100 wall balls** (previously 75). All divisions now perform 100 reps uniformly. | September 2024 (Cape Town event onward) |
| **SkiErg / Rower damper preset** | Damper is now preset to **Resistance 6** for all divisions. Racers may still adjust it. Previously this was not standardised. | 2025/26 season |
| **Rower foot plates preset** | Foot plates preset to **Position 4**. Racers may adjust. | 2025/26 season |
| **Sled Pull: no stepping on front line** | Athletes must **not step on the solid white line** at the front of the Racer's Box while holding the rope. | 2025/26 season |
| **Burpee Broad Jump clarification** | Athletes are now explicitly **permitted to use a knee** when stepping up from the bottom burpee position. | 2025/26 season |
| **Distance penalties removed** | For sleds, BBJ, and sandbag lunges, there are **no more distance-based penalties**. Instead: 1 warning, then **15-second time penalty** per subsequent infringement. | 2025/26 season |
| **Farmers Carry wrong weight** | Must **redo the entire station** with correct weight. Failure to do so = DQ. | 2025/26 season |
| **Sandbag cannot be put down** | Sandbag must remain on both shoulders throughout. First infringement = **15-second penalty** (no warning). Second infringement = **DQ**. | 2025/26 season |
| **Spitting / nose clearing** | Now explicitly penalised: **2 min per infringement**. | 2025/26 season |
| **Active cooling prohibited** | Water at aid stations is **for drinking only**. Pouring over body = **2 min penalty**. | 2025/26 season |
| **Wave start DQ** | Starting in an incorrect wave = **automatic DQ** (previously unclear). | 2025/26 season |
| **Doubles separation limit** | If a doubles team receives more than **3 infringements** for being too far apart, they are **DQ'd** (previously unlimited warnings). | 2025/26 season |
| **Doubles age groups realigned** | Now structured in **5-year increments** to match Singles age groups. | June 2025 onward |
| **Pro divisions extended to 60-69** | 60-64 and 65-69 age groups now get official Pro rankings. However, WC qualification for 60+ remains in Open only. | 2025/26 season |
| **Digital wall ball targets** | Some venues now use **automatic digital rep counters** on wall ball rigs. | Rolling deployment |
| **Shoes rule** | Shoes can be removed only at Wall Balls. Must be placed under rig and carried to finisher stage. | 2025/26 season |

*(Sources: Official HYROX 25/26 Rulebook; roxlyfe.com 2025/26 rulebook analysis; roxlyfe.com world records page notation)*

### 2.3 Race Time Breakdown: Where Is Time Spent?

#### Scientific Data (Brandt et al., 2025 — Frontiers in Physiology)

A peer-reviewed study of 11 recreational HYROX athletes (median finish time 86.5 min, Individual Open Division) found:

| Component | Median Time | % of Total Race |
|-----------|-------------|-----------------|
| **Total Running (8 km)** | 51.2 min | **~59%** |
| **Total Stations (8 stations)** | 32.8 min | **~38%** |
| **Roxzone / Transitions** | ~3–7 min (included in above) | **~3–7%** |
| **Full Race** | 86.5 min | 100% |

**Key finding:** Running time was **significantly longer** than station time (p = 0.003). Running accounts for approximately **50–60%** of total race time across all ability levels, with the percentage being slightly higher for slower athletes (who degrade more on later runs).

#### Elite vs. Average Breakdown (Roxlyfe.com Analysis — Pro Division)

| Component | Elite Men (~59 min) | Average Men (~90 min) | Elite Women (~66 min) | Average Women (~90 min) |
|-----------|--------------------|-----------------------|----------------------|-----------------------|
| **Total Running** | 30:46 (52%) | 42:26 (48%) | 34:27 (52%) | 44:09 (49%) |
| **Total Stations** | 25:10 (43%) | 39:50 (45%) | 28:48 (43%) | 39:49 (44%) |
| **Roxzone** | 2:54 (5%) | 6:58 (8%) | 3:47 (6%) | 6:12 (7%) |
| **Total** | 58:50 | 89:14 | 66:22 | 90:11 |

*(Source: roxlyfe.com "From Average to Elite" analysis)*

**Critical insight:** Running takes roughly **50–55%** of total time for elites and **48–50%** for average athletes (since slower athletes lose proportionally more time at stations). The Roxzone is **5–6% for elites** but balloons to **7–8%** for average athletes.

#### Station Time Rankings (Which Stations Take Longest)

Based on data from hyroxdatalab.com (200,000+ results) and the roxlyfe.com elite analysis:

**For recreational athletes (finishing ~1:30–1:40), from longest to shortest station time:**

| Rank | Station | Typical Time (Men, ~1:40 bracket) | Typical Time (Women, ~1:40 bracket) |
|------|---------|----------------------------------|-------------------------------------|
| 1 | **Wall Balls** | 8:02 | 6:30 |
| 2 | **Sled Pull** | 6:31 | 6:36 |
| 3 | **Burpee Broad Jump** | 5:15 | 6:00+ |
| 4 | **Sandbag Lunges** | 5:22 | 5:25 |
| 5 | **Rowing** | 4:35 | 5:12 |
| 6 | **SkiErg** | 4:17 | 4:51 |
| 7 | **Sled Push** | 3:40 | 3:48 |
| 8 | **Farmers Carry** | 2:32 | 2:45 |

**For elite athletes (finishing ~55–60 min):**

| Rank | Station | Typical Time (Elite Men) | Typical Time (Elite Women) |
|------|---------|--------------------------|---------------------------|
| 1 | **Wall Balls** | 4:25 | 3:50 |
| 2 | **Rowing** | 3:58 | 4:29 |
| 3 | **SkiErg** | 3:47 | 4:12 |
| 4 | **Sled Pull** | 3:14 | 3:54 |
| 5 | **Sandbag Lunges** | 3:03 | 3:35 |
| 6 | **Sled Push** | 2:45 | 3:00 |
| 7 | **Burpee Broad Jump** | 2:21 | 3:11 |
| 8 | **Farmers Carry** | 1:37 | 1:57 |

*(Sources: roxlyfe.com "From Average to Elite"; hyroxdatalab.com station analysis)*

### 2.4 The Biggest "Time Sinks" — Recreational vs. Elite

The **variance analysis** from hyroxdatalab.com (comparing 1:20 "advanced" to 1:40 "recreational" brackets) reveals which stations create the largest time gaps:

| Station | Time Variance (Men) | Time Variance (Women) | Priority Level |
|---------|--------------------|-----------------------|----------------|
| **Wall Balls** | **2:26** | **2:02** | 🔴 **HIGH** |
| **Roxzone (Total Transitions)** | **2:24** | **1:48** | 🔴 **HIGH** |
| **Burpee Broad Jump** | **1:47** | **2:08** | 🔴 **HIGH** |
| **Sandbag Lunges** | 1:27 | ~1:20 | 🟡 MEDIUM |
| **Sled Pull** | 1:16 | ~1:10 | 🟡 MEDIUM |
| **Sled Push** | 1:04 | ~0:50 | 🟡 MEDIUM |
| **Rowing** | 0:28 | ~0:30 | 🟢 LOW |
| **Farmers Carry** | 0:27 | ~0:25 | 🟢 LOW |
| **SkiErg** | 0:23 | ~0:25 | 🟢 LOW |

**Interpretation for coaches:**

- **Wall Balls** are the single biggest differentiator. A recreational male athlete averaging 8:02 vs. an advanced athlete at 5:36 — that's nearly **2.5 minutes** on one station alone. This is because wall balls demand sustained muscular endurance across 100 reps, and technique degrades rapidly under fatigue. A modest 20% improvement saves ~90 seconds.
- **Roxzone efficiency** is the "hidden" time sink. Elite athletes average **~28 seconds per transition** vs. ~52 seconds for recreational athletes. Over 8 transitions, that's **3:12 wasted** — with zero fitness required to improve it, just urgency and efficiency.
- **Burpee Broad Jumps** are the third-largest separator. They demand a unique combination of power, coordination, and cardio endurance that disproportionately punishes less fit athletes.
- **SkiErg, Rowing, and Farmers Carry** show the **smallest** variance. These are more "democratic" stations where technique and equipment constraints limit how much faster anyone can go. Focusing training time here yields diminishing returns.

The roxlyfe.com elite analysis shows an even more dramatic picture for the Sled Pull: elite men take 3:14 while average men take **6:31** — a ratio of 1:2, compared to a 1:1.3 ratio on Sled Push. The Sled Pull is disproportionately punishing for less-prepared athletes.

*(Sources: hyroxdatalab.com "Station Performance Analysis"; roxlyfe.com "From Average to Elite")*

### 2.5 Performance Tiers — Detailed Breakdown

Based on data from hyroxdatalab.com (700,000+ results), roxlyfe.com, Men's Health UK, and the scientific literature.

#### Tier Overview Table (Men's Open / Women's Open)

| Tier | Men's Time | Women's Time | Percentile | Running Pace (avg/km) | Typical Profile |
|------|-----------|-------------|------------|----------------------|-----------------|
| **World Class** | < 55 min | < 58 min | Top 0.1% | 3:30–3:50/km | Full-time HYROX athletes, Elite 15 competitors |
| **Elite** | 55–75 min | 58–84 min | Top 10% | 4:00–4:50/km | Competitive hybrid athletes, age group podiums |
| **Advanced** | 1:15–1:25 | 1:26–1:38 | Top 10–25% | 4:50–5:15/km | Dedicated training 5–6×/week, 2+ years HYROX experience |
| **Intermediate** | 1:25–1:40 | 1:38–1:54 | 25–50th % | 5:15–5:45/km | Consistent training 4–5×/week, knows all stations |
| **Beginner** | 1:40–1:54 | 1:54–2:10 | 50–75th % | 5:45–6:30/km | First or second race, general fitness background |
| **Finisher** | 1:54+ | 2:10+ | 75th+ % | 6:30+/km | New to fitness racing, completion-focused |

*(Source: hyroxdatalab.com "What is a Good HYROX Time?")*

#### Tier 1: Sub-60 Minutes (World Class / Elite Pro)

- **Who:** Full-time HYROX athletes competing in the Elite 15 series. Names like Alexander Roncevic (53:15 Men's Pro), Joanna Wietrzyk (56:03 Women's Pro), Lauren Weeks, Hunter McIntyre.
- **Running pace:** 3:30–4:00/km average across all 8 runs. Remarkably consistent pacing — first km at ~3:24, last km at ~4:15 (men's elite). The pace degradation is minimal (~50 seconds from first to last km).
- **Station characteristics:**
  - SkiErg: 3:40–4:00
  - Sled Push: 2:30–3:00
  - Sled Pull: 3:00–3:30
  - Burpee Broad Jumps: 2:15–3:00
  - Rowing: 3:45–4:10
  - Farmers Carry: 1:30–1:50
  - Sandbag Lunges: 2:50–3:20
  - Wall Balls: 3:45–4:30
- **Roxzone:** Total ~2:30–3:30. Average per transition: **~20–25 seconds**. They treat Roxzone as running — zero standing still.
- **Fitness characteristics:** VO₂max likely 55–70+ mL/kg/min. Sub-35 min 10K runners. Capable of 150+ kg deadlift. 100 wall balls unbroken in under 4:30 in training. Compromised running ability is exceptional — can maintain 4:00/km pace immediately after heavy sled work.
- **Training:** 8–12 sessions/week. Periodised with specific HYROX simulation blocks. Race-specific pacing work. 60–80 km running per week.

#### Tier 2: 60–75 Minutes (Competitive / Strong Recreational)

- **Who:** Experienced HYROX racers (3+ races), competitive age group athletes, former runners or CrossFitters who've adapted well.
- **Running pace:** 4:15–5:00/km. Moderate pace degradation — typically lose ~1:00–1:30 from first to last km.
- **Station characteristics:**
  - SkiErg: 4:00–4:30
  - Sled Push: 3:00–3:30
  - Sled Pull: 3:30–4:45
  - Burpee Broad Jumps: 3:00–4:45
  - Rowing: 4:00–4:40
  - Farmers Carry: 1:45–2:10
  - Sandbag Lunges: 3:20–4:30
  - Wall Balls: 5:00–6:15
- **Roxzone:** Total ~4:00–5:30. Average per transition: ~30–40 seconds.
- **Fitness characteristics:** VO₂max approximately 48–58 mL/kg/min. 5K time of 19–22 min. Solid general strength (bodyweight back squat, 1.5× bodyweight deadlift). Can complete 100 wall balls in 5–6 min fresh. Good but not elite compromised running.
- **Training:** 5–6 sessions/week. Blend of running (40–60 km/week), HYROX-specific station work 2–3×/week, and strength training 2–3×/week.

#### Tier 3: 75–90 Minutes (Solid Recreational)

- **Who:** Athletes with general fitness backgrounds. Often 2nd–4th HYROX race. May have a running OR strength bias but not both.
- **Running pace:** 5:00–5:45/km. Significant pace degradation — runs 6, 7, and 8 are often 60–90 seconds slower than runs 1–2.
- **Station characteristics:**
  - SkiErg: 4:15–4:50
  - Sled Push: 3:20–4:00
  - Sled Pull: 4:30–6:00 (sled pull is often where strength-deficient athletes struggle badly)
  - Burpee Broad Jumps: 4:30–6:00
  - Rowing: 4:30–5:15
  - Farmers Carry: 2:00–2:30
  - Sandbag Lunges: 4:00–5:30
  - Wall Balls: 6:00–7:30
- **Roxzone:** Total ~5:30–7:30. Average per transition: ~40–55 seconds. Often includes conscious "rest" pauses, water stops, and mental resets.
- **Fitness characteristics:** VO₂max approximately 40–50 mL/kg/min. 5K time of 22–26 min. Moderate strength levels. Wall balls may require 3–5 rest breaks during the set. Compromised running is a weakness — HR doesn't settle between stations.
- **Training:** 3–5 sessions/week. General fitness with some HYROX-specific prep. Running 20–40 km/week.

#### Tier 4: 90+ Minutes (Beginner / Completion-Focused)

- **Who:** First-time HYROX racers, general fitness enthusiasts, those training for completion not competition.
- **Running pace:** 5:45–7:00+/km. Massive pace degradation is common. Run 1 may be 5:00/km but Run 8 can exceed 7:00/km. Walking intervals common in later runs.
- **Station characteristics:**
  - SkiErg: 4:45–5:30+
  - Sled Push: 3:45–5:00+ (may need to rest mid-push on heavy sleds)
  - Sled Pull: 5:30–8:00+ (this station can become a major bottleneck; athletes may need 7+ minutes)
  - Burpee Broad Jumps: 5:30–8:00+
  - Rowing: 4:45–5:45
  - Farmers Carry: 2:20–3:15+ (grip failures, need to put down kettlebells multiple times)
  - Sandbag Lunges: 5:00–7:00+
  - Wall Balls: 7:00–10:00+ (frequent rest breaks, technique deterioration, no-reps)
- **Roxzone:** Total ~7:00–12:00+. Average per transition: ~52–90 seconds. Extended rest periods, deliberate water breaks, mental regrouping.
- **Fitness characteristics:** VO₂max approximately 35–45 mL/kg/min. 5K time of 26–32+ min. Strength may be limited — sled push/pull and wall balls feel genuinely heavy. Heart rate remains very elevated (>85% HRmax for most of race). Blood lactate peaks at wall balls (the final station) — research shows RPE reaches 18/20 (Borg scale) during wall balls for recreational athletes.
- **Training:** 2–4 sessions/week of general fitness. Limited HYROX-specific preparation. First-timers often improve **15–25%** from first to second race simply through experience, pacing knowledge, and station familiarity.

*(Sources: hyroxdatalab.com tier analysis; roxlyfe.com pace breakdowns; Brandt et al. 2025 Frontiers in Physiology; Men's Health UK station time analysis)*

### 2.6 Typical Progression Timeline

Based on hyroxdatalab.com's progression data for a typical male athlete aged 30–34:

| Stage | Finish Time | Timeframe |
|-------|-------------|-----------|
| First race | ~1:55:00 (beginner) | Day 1 |
| 6 months later | ~1:40:00 (intermediate) | +6 months (~13% improvement) |
| 1 year later | ~1:25:00 (advanced) | +1 year (~15% improvement) |
| 2 years later | ~1:15:00 (elite) | +2 years (~12% improvement) |
| 3+ years | 1:10–1:14 | Peak elite performance, marginal gains |

Most athletes plateau after **3–5 years** unless they significantly alter their training approach.

| Division | Average Finish Time |
|----------|-------------------|
| Men's Pro | 1:22:24 |
| Men's Open | 1:26:42 |
| Women's Open | ~1:38:02 |
| All finishers (both genders) | ~1:35–1:40 (men), ~1:47–1:54 (women) |
| Median (50th percentile) Men | 1:33–1:38 |
| Median (50th percentile) Women | 1:47–1:52 |

*(Sources: Men's Health UK citing RoxHype data 2025; hyroxdatalab.com; roxlyfe.com)*

### 2.8 Station Benchmark Times by Performance Level (Men / Women)

| Station | Elite (M / W) | Advanced (M / W) | Intermediate (M / W) | Recreational (M / W) |
|---------|---------------|-------------------|----------------------|-----------------------|
| SkiErg | 3:50 / 4:30 | 4:20 / 5:00 | 4:27 / 5:11 | 4:50+ / 5:30+ |
| Sled Push | 2:50 / 2:50 | 3:26 / 3:25 | 3:41 / 3:42 | 4:00+ / 4:00+ |
| Sled Pull | 3:50 / 4:15 | 4:37 / 4:59 | 5:06 / 5:34 | 6:00+ / 6:00+ |
| Burpee Broad Jump | 4:00 / 5:15 | 4:37 / 5:57 | 5:19 / 6:50 | 6:00+ / 7:30+ |
| Rowing | 4:00 / 4:45 | 4:33 / 5:11 | 4:44 / 5:24 | 5:00+ / 5:45+ |
| Farmers Carry | 1:45 / 2:00 | 1:59 / 2:15 | 2:10 / 2:25 | 2:30+ / 2:45+ |
| Lunges | 3:50 / 4:00 | 4:24 / 4:30 | 4:56 / 5:01 | 5:30+ / 5:30+ |
| Wall Balls | 5:30 / 5:20 | 6:04 / 5:53 | 7:01 / 6:51 | 8:00+ / 7:30+ |

*(Source: hyroxdatalab.com "What Is a Good HYROX Time?" benchmark tables)*

### 2.9 Physiological Demands Summary

From Brandt et al. (2025), the first peer-reviewed HYROX study:

| Metric | Value | Context |
|--------|-------|---------|
| HR max during race | 185 bpm (median) | Significantly higher during stations than runs |
| HR average during race | 170.9 bpm | Consistently hard to very hard intensity |
| % of race at "very hard" intensity (>90% HRmax) | 79.5% | Dominant intensity zone |
| % of race at "hard" intensity (70-90% HRmax) | 19.6% | — |
| Blood lactate max | 8.5 mmol/L | Peaked during wall balls (final station) |
| Blood lactate avg | 6.3 mmol/L | Sustained moderate-high lactate throughout |
| RPE max (Borg scale) | 18 / 20 | Highest at wall balls |
| Strongest performance predictor | VO₂max (ρ = -0.71) | Aerobic capacity is king |
| Second predictor | Body fat % (ρ = 0.67) | Lower body fat = faster time |
| Third predictor | Endurance training volume (ρ = -0.68) | More endurance training = better |
| Strength correlation | **Not significant** (p > 0.05) | HGS, muscle mass % did not correlate with total time |

**Key coaching implication:** HYROX is fundamentally an **endurance event** with strength components, not a strength event with running. The scientific data shows that once athletes have sufficient strength to handle the competition loads, further aerobic capacity development is the primary path to faster times. However, station-specific work remains critical for the high-variance stations (wall balls, burpee broad jumps, sled pull).

### 2.10 Training Time Allocation Recommendation (Based on Data)

The hyroxdatalab.com "70/30 Strategy" and roxlyfe.com analysis converge on the following evidence-based training allocation:

| Training Focus | Allocation | Rationale |
|---------------|------------|-----------|
| **Aerobic Base / Running** | 40–50% of total training | Running is 50–55% of race time. VO₂max is the #1 predictor. |
| **High-Variance Station Work** (Wall Balls, Burpee Broad Jumps, Sled Pull) | 25–30% of total training | These 3 stations + Roxzone account for **6–8 minutes** of potential time savings. |
| **Medium-Variance Station Work** (Sled Push, Sandbag Lunges) | 10–15% of total training | Moderate improvement opportunity (3–4 min savings). |
| **Low-Variance Station Work** (SkiErg, Rowing, Farmers Carry) | 5–10% of total training | Important for technique but limited time-saving leverage (1–2 min). |
| **Compromised Running Practice** | Embedded in above | Running immediately after station work is a critical HYROX-specific skill. |
| **Roxzone / Transition Practice** | Mental + habitual | "Free" time savings — requires urgency and efficiency, not fitness. Target <6.5% of total race time. |

*(Sources: hyroxdatalab.com "Station Performance Analysis" 70/30 strategy; roxlyfe.com coaching recommendations; Brandt et al. 2025 training implications)*

---

*This document was compiled from the Official HYROX 25/26 Season Rulebook (Singles and Doubles), roxlyfe.com world records and analysis articles, hyroxdatalab.com (200,000+ and 700,000+ result datasets), hybridfitnessmedia.com, pace-club.com weight references, Concept2.com equipment specifications, fitnessexperiment.co course layout analysis, warriorperformancelab.com doubles guide, Men's Health UK station time reporting, and Brandt et al. (2025) "Acute physiological responses and performance determinants in Hyrox©" published in Frontiers in Physiology (PMC11994925). All data current as of February 2026.*

Now I have comprehensive data from multiple sources. Let me compile the final reference document.
