# Commercial Training Program Analysis for Hyrox Race Preparation

*Research Report for AI Coaching System Development*

---

## 1. PRVN (Proven Training — Tia-Clair Toomey & Shane Orr)

### Creator/Origin

**Correction on attribution:** Based on the research data, PRVN Fitness is built on the expertise of **Tia-Clair Toomey** (7x Fittest Woman on Earth, not Kara Saunders) and her husband/coach **Shane Orr**, one of the most decorated coaches in CrossFit history. The program operates out of PRVN Nashville (2600 Fessey Park Rd, Nashville, TN 37204) and has expanded aggressively into HYROX-specific programming, affiliate programming, supplement sales, and apparel. PRVN describes its mission as empowering "as many people across the globe to reach new heights and become PRVN" (Source: BTWB Programs page).

### Program Overview & Tiers

PRVN offers a multi-track ecosystem delivered through both the BTWB app and the Wodify Marketplace:

| Track | Frequency | Target Audience | Description |
|-------|-----------|-----------------|-------------|
| **PRVN Affiliate** | 6 days/week, 60-min sessions | GPP community (beginner to advanced) | Full class plans with coaching notes, warm-ups, primers, WODs, mobility, accessories |
| **PRVN Competitor** | Add-on sessions | Competitive athletes | Extra conditioning and lift frequency; can be scheduled before/after main class |
| **PRVN HYROX** | Daily programming | HYROX athletes of all levels | 8-week structured cycles, race day prep, year-round training |
| **PRVN HYROX Base** | Reduced frequency | Busy athletes | Condensed HYROX track |
| **PRVN Burn** | 2 days/week | All levels | Stamina, aerobic capacity, muscular endurance; low barrier to entry |
| **PRVN Olympic Lifting** | 3 days/week | Technique-focused athletes | Mechanics, technique, proficiency toward new 1RMs |
| **PRVN Gymnastics** | 2 days/week | Skill development | Gymnastics strength and skill progressions |
| **PRVN Bodybuilding** | 3 days/week | Aesthetics/joint health | Classic bodybuilding for aesthetics and structural resilience |

**Cost:** PRVN HYROX starts at **$45/month** with discounts for longer commitments (3-month at $128, 6-month at $243, yearly at $432 — representing up to 20% savings). All plans include a 7-day free trial. Affiliate programming is subscription-based through Rogue/BTWB (Source: prvnfitness.com, roguefitness.com).

### Weekly Template and Training Split

Based on the CrossFit Coorparoo affiliate implementation of PRVN programming, the weekly structure follows a deliberate thematic approach:

| Day | Theme | Primary Focus | Secondary Focus |
|-----|-------|---------------|-----------------|
| **Monday** | Battery Work / Absolute Strength | Back Squat 5RM or EMOM couplet | 15:00+ AMRAP or conditioning |
| **Tuesday** | Cyclical Upper Body Interference | Gymnastics skills (e.g., Ring MU) | Interval conditioning (4 × 5:00 AMRAP / 2:30 rest) |
| **Wednesday** | Absolute Leg Strength | Heavy barbell work (Back Squat heavy 3s) | Leg stamina triplet (8:00 AMRAP) |
| **Thursday** | Aerobic/Bodyweight Focus | Mixed modal endurance | Active flush / aerobic base (e.g., Every 3:00 × 10 sets) |
| **Friday** | Olympic Lifting + Sprint Tester | Snatch/Clean complexes | Sprint chipper "For Time" |
| **Saturday** | Upper Push / Lower Pull | Team-style EMOM (Bench + DL + Bike) | Community/team format |
| **Sunday** | Full Body CrossFit Pump | Interval work (Out and Back) | Strength EMOM or varied movements |

(Source: CrossFit Coorparoo PRVN Weekly Programming, Jan 25, 2025)

### Session Format

Each PRVN Affiliate session follows a tightly managed **60-minute class structure**:

| Time Block | Component | Duration |
|------------|-----------|----------|
| 0:00–3:00 | Whiteboard brief | 3 min |
| 3:00–12:00 | Warm-up (movement-specific) | 9 min |
| 12:00–18:00 | Barbell Primer / Skill Progression | 6 min |
| 18:00–23:00 | Build to working loads | 5 min |
| 23:00–35:00 | Weightlifting / Strength piece | 12 min |
| 35:00–40:00 | Transition | 5 min |
| 40:00–52:00 | WOD / Conditioning | 12 min |
| 52:00–55:00 | Clean-up | 3 min |
| 55:00–60:00 | Mobility + Cool Down | 5 min |

**Key structural features:**
- Warm-ups are built around **intended muscle group activation**, range of motion, and muscle imbalance prevention
- Every day includes **skill progressions and technique primers** specific to beginners through elite
- **Mobility is integrated** into the 60-minute class (not optional post-class)
- Optional **bulletproofing/accessory** work is provided for athletes to do on their own time
- **Multiple scaling levels** (Level 1, 2, 3) are provided for WODs with distinct loading and rep prescriptions

(Source: BTWB Programs page, Rogue Fitness product page)

### Progression Model

PRVN programs in named **cycles** (e.g., "Artemis Cycle," "Poseidon Cycle") with clear periodization:

- **Powerlifting:** 5-3-1 style progression focused on maintaining strength in critical rep ranges (Back Squat, Strict Press, Deadlift toward 1RM testing)
- **Weightlifting:** Alternating weekly focus — complexes for technique building and familiarity with ~3RM/ladder work, progressing from hang positional work to power variations to full lifts
- **Gymnastics:** Strict strength development → high skill integration → Murph prep
- **Conditioning:** Balanced across time domains — one workout/week targeting 7–11 min, one at 11–15 min, one at 20+ min, plus intervals and EMOMs for capacity
- **Transition phases** align with the CrossFit Open (3-week transition), front-loading strength and back-loading Open workout intensity
- **HYROX track** uses structured **8-week cycles** year-round

(Source: CFC/PRVN Programming 24th–2nd, Feb 2025)

### Representative Sample Workouts

**Workout 1: Weightlifting + WOD (Sample Day from BTWB/Rogue)**

*Warm-Up:*
- 2 rounds for quality: 1 min cardio choice, 8L/8R Single Leg RDLs, 10 Alt Goblet Cossack Squats, 6 Inchworm Push-Ups, 10 Mountain Climber Lunges

*Barbell Primer:*
- 5 sets: 1 Clean Lift Off + 1 Slow Muscle Clean + 1 Low Hang Power Clean + 1 Hang Squat Clean (building weight)

*Weightlifting:*
- Every 2:00 × 6 sets: [1 Clean Pull + 1 Power Clean + 1 Squat Clean]
  - Sets 1–2: @75% 1RM Squat Clean
  - Set 3: @80%
  - Set 4: @85%
  - Set 5: @87+%
  - Set 6: Heavy for the day

*WOD — "Bowser" (Level 2):*
- Every 1:00 × 6 min alternating: 6 Hang Power Cleans @65–70% 1RM / 15/11 Bike Calories
- *Then* — Every 1:00 × 6 min alternating: 4 Hang Power Cleans @70–75% 1RM / 15/11 Bike Calories

*Mobility:* Elevated Pigeon Stretch 2 min/side, Weighted Standing Straddle 2 min, Couch Stretch 1 min/side, Weighted Ankle Stretch 1 min/side

*Accessories:* 4 rounds for quality: 100m Farmer Carry (pick load), L100ft/R100ft Crossover Sled Drag, 30s KB Dead Bug

**Workout 2: Battery Work Monday**
- 21:00 EMOM Couplet: Burpee Box Jump Overs + Clean Complex (1 Clean + 1 Hang Clean)

**Workout 3: Absolute Leg Strength Wednesday**
- *Strength:* Back Squat — Heavy sets of 3 (absolute strength focus)
- *Conditioning:* 8:00 AMRAP: DB Power Cleans + DB Reverse Lunges + Double Unders

**Workout 4: Aerobic/Bodyweight Thursday**
- Every 3:00 × 10 sets, alternating stations: Station A — Run + Burpees; Station B — Row + Wall Walks

**Workout 5: Sprint Chipper Friday**
- *Olympic Lifting:* Snatch Pull + Snatch (progressive loading)
- *WOD — For Time:* Wall Balls + Chest-to-Bar Pull-Ups + Power Snatches (sprint chipper format)

### Hyrox Applicability Analysis

**What Transfers Well:**
- **PRVN HYROX track** is purpose-built — 8-week cycles, daily programming, race-day priming protocols, and leveled scaling make this a direct fit
- The **Affiliate program's conditioning structure** (balanced time domains from 7–11 min through 20+ min) mirrors the varied demands of Hyrox (roughly 60–90 min race with alternating running and functional stations)
- **EMOM and interval formatting** (e.g., "Bowser") closely replicates the work:rest pacing demands of transitioning between Hyrox running segments and stations
- **Sled work** is explicitly programmed (Crossover Sled Drags in accessories), which is one of the most Hyrox-specific movements
- **Farmer carries** are regularly included in accessory work
- **Multi-level scaling** (Levels 1/2/3) allows an AI coach to auto-scale based on athlete profile
- **Cyclical endurance sessions** (Thursday aerobic focus with running + rowing) build the aerobic base Hyrox demands

**What's Missing or Needs Modification:**
- The **Affiliate track prioritizes CrossFit competition movements** (Ring Muscle-Ups, Chest-to-Bar Pull-Ups, Snatches) that have zero Hyrox transfer
- **Running volume is insufficient** for Hyrox prep — Thursday is the primary running day, but Hyrox athletes need 3–4 dedicated running sessions per week
- **Olympic lifting frequency** is higher than necessary for Hyrox; that time would be better spent on rowing/ski erg/bike intervals and running progressions
- **Wall balls** are programmed but not at Hyrox-specific standards (100 reps at specific target height)
- **Burpee broad jumps** are absent from most sample programming
- **SkiErg** is available but not emphasized in the way Hyrox demands

**Modification for 16-Week Hyrox Prep:**
1. Replace Olympic lifting days with Hyrox-specific station practice (wall balls ×100, sled push/pull, rowing 1km, burpee broad jumps ×80m)
2. Add 2–3 weekly running sessions at varied intensities (Zone 2 base, tempo, race-pace intervals)
3. Retain the EMOM/interval conditioning format but swap CrossFit movements for Hyrox station movements
4. Keep the 5-3-1 strength progression but focus on squat, deadlift, and lunges (eliminate strict press emphasis)
5. Use the PRVN HYROX track directly if available, supplementing with additional running volume

### Key Programming Principles for AI Coach Extraction

1. **Themed daily structure** with clear intent (strength day, aerobic day, sprint day) — the AI should assign a daily purpose
2. **Multi-level scaling** (Level 1/2/3) based on athlete capability — the AI should auto-prescribe the appropriate level
3. **Percentage-based strength work** building through 5-3-1 progressions to 1RM testing
4. **Named training cycles** with transition phases — the AI should plan in 6–8 week mesocycles
5. **60-minute session architecture** with time blocks — the AI should structure every session with warm-up, primer, main work, conditioning, and mobility
6. **Balanced time-domain exposure** across the week (short sprint, medium grind, long endurance)
7. **Integrated mobility** within the session, not optional afterthought

---

## 2. HWPO (Hard Work Pays Off — Mat Fraser)

### Program Overview

HWPO Training is Mat Fraser's post-retirement programming platform, launched after his fifth consecutive CrossFit Games championship. The platform has grown into a comprehensive multi-tier system targeting athletes from casual fitness enthusiasts to elite competitors.

| Program | Duration/Session | Frequency | Target Athlete | Monthly Cost |
|---------|-----------------|-----------|----------------|-------------|
| **HWPO Flagship 2.0** | ~2 hours | 4–6 days/week | Experienced CrossFitters seeking PRs | $40/month |
| **Flagship 60** | ~60 minutes | Same schedule | Time-constrained athletes | Included with Flagship |
| **Flagship Masters** | Adjusted volume | Same schedule | Advancing athletes prioritizing longevity | Included with Flagship |
| **HWPO PRO** | 2–3 hours × 2 sessions/day | 6 days/week | Top 300 Quarterfinal athletes | Separate pricing |
| **HWPO Classic** | Varies | Daily | Community daily WOD (non-progressive) | ~$20/month |
| **HWPO Sweat** | 45 minutes | Varies | Minimal equipment, general fitness | ~$20/month |
| **HWPO Strong 2.0** | 60–75 minutes | Varies | Strength-focused with optional metcon | Separate pricing |
| **ALL ACCESS** | All programs | All | Flexible goal-changers | $49/month or $490/year |

(Sources: hwpotraining.com, Rogue Fitness, garagegymrevisited.com, mensfitnesstoday.com)

### Core Philosophy

Fraser's programming philosophy centers on several principles derived from his competitive career:

1. **Percentage-based progression:** All strength training is based on 1RM percentages, with RPE tools available for athletes who haven't yet tested maxes. This ensures individualization at scale.
2. **Phase-based structure aligned to the CrossFit season:** Flagship 2.0 follows "thoughtfully designed PHASES that progress strength and work capacity, tailored to the CROSSFIT SEASON" culminating with the Open and Quarterfinals.
3. **Community synchronization:** Unlike the original Flagship (where everyone started on Day 1 regardless of join date), Flagship 2.0 has all athletes on the same training day for "better coaching support, real-time leaderboards, and sharing your fitness journey."
4. **Deload intelligence:** The program uses 4-week blocks with 3 weeks on and 1 deload week. Two 4-week blocks form an 8-week cycle, and the macro structure operates in 16-week super-cycles (16-16-16).
5. **Intensity through forced breaks:** Rather than long unbroken AMRAPs, Fraser programs short work windows with built-in rest (e.g., 4 × 2-min AMRAPs with 1-min rest) to force higher intensity output per window.

(Sources: garagegymrevisited.com, YouTube review transcript, hwpotraining.com)

### Weekly Template

**HWPO Flagship 2.0 Typical Week:**

| Day | Components | Approximate Duration |
|-----|------------|---------------------|
| **Day 1** | Warm-up → Squats (heavy) + Olympic Lift → Metcon → Accessories → (Bonus) | ~2 hours |
| **Day 2** | Warm-up → Front Squats (lighter) + Pressing → Rowing/Bike piece → Accessories | ~2 hours |
| **Day 3** | Warm-up → Deadlift + Olympic Lift → Metcon → Accessories → (Bonus) | ~2 hours |
| **Day 4** | Warm-up → Bench Press + Gymnastics → Conditioning piece → Accessories | ~1.5–2 hours |
| **Day 5** | Warm-up → 40-min EMOM or longer conditioning → Accessories | ~1.5–2 hours |
| **Day 6** | Active recovery: light spin bike, swimming, or easy run | 30–60 min |
| **Day 7** | Full rest | — |

**Key structural patterns:**
- **Squats 2×/week:** One heavy back squat day, one lighter front squat day
- **Deadlifts 1×/week**
- **Bench press 1×/week**
- **Olympic lifts ~3×/week** with volume varying by cycle
- **Rowing appears heavily** throughout — Fraser is a known rowing advocate
- **10–22+ working strength sets** per session before conditioning
- **Metcons last 12–20 minutes** typically
- **Accessories always present;** bonus work (often Zone 2 cardio) is optional

(Source: garagegymrevisited.com)

### Session Structure: HWPO Flagship vs. Flagship 60 vs. PRO

**Flagship Session Architecture:**
1. Coaching video from Mat Fraser or staff coach (intent briefing)
2. Intentional warm-up (mimicking session movements)
3. Strength progressions with strength accessory work
4. Gymnastics progressions
5. Metcon OR monostructural conditioning (rowing, running, swimming)
6. Accessories
7. Optional bonus/extra workout (can add ~1 hour)

**Flagship 60** removes either a strength piece or accessory piece(s) from Flagship; occasionally shortens the metcon by 25–33% or lightens strength percentages slightly. Never exceeds 70 minutes including warm-up and clean-up.

**HWPO PRO** requires:
- 2 sessions/day, 3–4 hours total
- Top 300 Quarterfinal placement
- Specific strength minimums (245/155 lb Snatch, 275/185 lb C&J, 365 lb Back Squat)
- No modifications or scaling
- Access to track, pool, specialty equipment
- Off-Season and Comp Prep phases with track variations (Aerobic Focus track for athletes who struggle with longer metcons)

**HWPO Strong 2.0:**
- Each session: warm-up → primary lift → secondary lift → accessory work → optional metcon/conditioning
- 60–75 minutes per session
- 4–8 week blocks with deload every 4th week
- Hybrid percentage + RPE progression

(Sources: hwpotraining.com, thebarbellspin.com, roguefitness.com)

### Representative Sample Workouts

**Workout 1: HWPO Flagship — Week 2 Pressing Day (Published by Fraser, Men's Health)**

*Warm-Up (3 Rounds):*
- 15 Cal Ski Erg
- 10/10 Half-Kneeling Single-Arm DB Press
- 10 DB Romanian Deadlifts
- 4 Inchworms

*Strength A — Push Press:*
- 1 × 10 @57% 1RM
- 1 × 10 @60% 1RM
- 2 × 8 @63% 1RM

*Strength B — Strict Press:*
- 4 × 10 @90% of 10RM

*Metcon:*
- Buy-In: Tabata Bike (8 rounds: 20s on / 10s off)
- 5 Rounds: 8 Sandbag Cleans + 10 Burpees Over Sandbag
- Buy-Out: 20/16 Assault Bike Calories

*Accessories:*
- 4 × 20 Assisted Strict Pull-Ups
- 5 × 15 OH DB Triceps Extensions
- 3 × 15 Reverse Hypers (or Back Extensions)

*Bonus Work (separate session):*
- 40 minutes Spin Bike or Run in Zone 2 (145 BPM)

**Workout 2: HWPO Flagship — Typical Heavy Squat Day (Reconstructed from Review Data)**

*Warm-Up:* Movement-specific activation, 2–3 rounds
*Strength:* Back Squat — heavy sets (percentage-based, progressing through cycle)
- Example: 5 × 3 @82–88% 1RM (building across sets)
*Olympic Lift:* Power Clean or Snatch variation — 3–5 working sets
*Metcon:* 4 × 2:00 AMRAP with 1:00 rest — high-intensity work windows with mixed modality
*Accessories:* GHD work, single-leg variations

**Workout 3: HWPO — Saturday 40-Minute EMOM (Typical Long Conditioning)**
- 40:00 EMOM alternating stations:
  - Min 1: Row Calories
  - Min 2: Wall Balls
  - Min 3: KB Swings
  - Min 4: Box Jumps
  - (Repeat 10 rounds)
- Built-in intensity elements in 1–2 stations to prevent "cruise control"

**Workout 4: HWPO Sweat — Full Body (Published Sample)**
- 0:00–12:00 — EMOM 12:
  - 1a. Glute Bridge × 30s
  - 1b. Side Plank Hip Touch × 20s each side
  - 1c. Walking or Stationary Lunge × 30s
- (Followed by AMRAP conditioning and accessory circuit — minimal equipment)

**Workout 5: HWPO Strong 2.0 — Typical Session Structure**
- Warm-up: targeted activation
- Primary Lift: e.g., Back Squat 4 × 5 @75–82% (progressing week to week)
- Secondary Lift: e.g., Romanian Deadlift 3 × 8
- Accessory Work: 3–4 exercises (single-leg, core, posterior chain)
- Optional Metcon: 8–12 min conditioning piece
- *Deload week every 4th week*

### Hyrox Applicability Analysis

**What Transfers Well:**
- **Rowing dominance:** HWPO programs extensive rowing volume, which directly transfers to the 1km row station in Hyrox
- **Assault/Echo Bike work** is standard — transfers to the bike erg conditioning demands
- **Zone 2 bonus work** (40-min spin bike/run @145 BPM) is exactly the aerobic base work Hyrox athletes need
- **Sandbag cleans** appear in metcons — a direct Hyrox station movement
- **Wall balls** feature in conditioning pieces
- **Forced-break interval structure** (short AMRAPs with built-in rest) trains the ability to sustain high output across transitions, exactly like moving between Hyrox running and station segments
- **4-week block periodization with deloads** is directly applicable to a 16-week Hyrox prep (4 mesocycles)
- **Percentage-based strength work** keeps loading individualized and progressive
- **Strong 2.0's structure** (primary lift + secondary lift + optional metcon in 60–75 min) is an excellent template for Hyrox strength days

**What's Missing:**
- **Running volume is grossly insufficient** for Hyrox — running appears occasionally in metcons and as bonus Zone 2, but a Hyrox athlete needs 8km of total race running and should be running 20–30+ km/week in training
- **Olympic lifting takes up significant training time** with no Hyrox transfer (no snatches, cleans, or jerks in Hyrox)
- **Gymnastic skills** (muscle-ups, handstand walks, etc.) consume programming space with zero Hyrox applicability
- **Session length of ~2 hours** is problematic for time-constrained athletes; the Flagship 60 variant helps but still sacrifices running opportunities
- **Sled push/pull** — despite being the hardest Hyrox station for many athletes — appears to be underrepresented relative to its race importance
- **Burpee broad jumps** are not standard in HWPO programming
- **Ski erg** is programmed but not at Hyrox-specific distances/intensities (1km race segment)
- **Lunges** (particularly weighted walking lunges, a Hyrox station) don't appear with the specificity or volume Hyrox demands

**Modification for 16-Week Hyrox Prep:**
1. Use the **4-week block + deload structure** (4 mesocycles of 3+1)
2. Replace all Olympic lifting with Hyrox station practice and additional running
3. Keep the **squat, deadlift, and bench** strength progressions (excellent base for sled, lunge, and wall ball performance)
4. Expand running from bonus work to **3–4 dedicated sessions/week** at varying intensities
5. Adopt the **forced-break interval metcon format** but populate it with Hyrox movements
6. Use the **Flagship 60 or Strong 2.0 template** as the base structure to keep sessions manageable

### Key Programming Principles for AI Coach Extraction

1. **Phased periodization in 4-week blocks** with programmed deload weeks — the AI must auto-schedule deloads
2. **1RM percentage-based loading** with RPE fallback for untested athletes
3. **Coaching video/intent briefing model** — the AI should provide intent and stimulus descriptions for every session
4. **Forced-break interval design** to maximize intensity within work windows
5. **Community synchronization** (everyone on the same day) improves accountability — the AI should support cohort-based training
6. **Distinct tracks for different time budgets** (2-hour vs 60-min) — the AI needs a session-length selector that trims intelligently (remove accessories, shorten metcon, lighten percentages)
7. **Progressive onboarding** — new athletes start with introductory weeks before full-intensity programming
8. **Heavy emphasis on monostructural conditioning** (dedicated rowing, biking, running pieces separate from metcons)

---

## 3. CompTrain (Ben Bergeron)

### Program Overview

CompTrain is Ben Bergeron's programming platform, born from his 15 years coaching elite CrossFit Games athletes and his broader philosophy around gym programming as a retention and community-building tool. CompTrain positions itself explicitly as **gym programming** — designed for affiliate class settings rather than individual competitors.

**Program tiers:**

| Track | Format | Target Audience | Description |
|-------|--------|-----------------|-------------|
| **CompTrain Gym Programming** | 6 days/week class plans | Affiliate owners & coaches | Complete daily lesson plans with coaching notes, scaling, and class management |
| **Benchmark testing** | Every 2 weeks | All members | 24 repeated workouts/year for progress tracking |

CompTrain is available through the **Wodify Marketplace** and its own platform (comptrain.com). The programming is delivered as turnkey class plans that coaches can implement immediately.

**Key positioning difference:** While PRVN and HWPO are athlete-facing (individuals subscribe), CompTrain is primarily **gym-facing** (affiliate owners subscribe, members follow in class). Bergeron emphasizes that "programming is a retention tool" and that a dedicated employee handles programming creation while he reviews everything. (Source: YouTube interview)

### "Intentional Intensity" Philosophy

CompTrain's programming philosophy rests on several explicitly stated principles:

1. **Program for the majority, not the top 10%:** "Programming for the top 10% of your athletes and scaling for the rest doesn't work." The goal is workouts that are "doable but difficult for most" where the class does the same work together.

2. **Consistent weekly structure with variance in workouts:** A "predictable rhythm to the schedule" that members can build routines around, while the specific movements and loadings change.

3. **Concurrent development:** "Rather than focusing on building strength one month, endurance in another, and high-intensity capacity in the next, we build them together every week and all year round." This is a fundamentally different periodization approach from PRVN and HWPO's blocked phases.

4. **Intentional intensity:** "Intensity drives results, but when structured poorly and without intelligent controls around volume, it can become the barrier to progress." CompTrain implements this through "movement pairings, loading, & rep schemes that fall into our programming sweet spot for sustainable power output."

5. **No complex gymnastics:** "We don't program complex gymnastic movements... The reality of your member's lives demands strength, endurance, and capacity. It doesn't require them to know how to walk on their hands."

6. **Running as a cornerstone:** Programming includes "running 2-3 times a week at varying intensities and distances" — significantly more running emphasis than most CrossFit programming platforms.

7. **Benchmark testing every 2 weeks:** 24 workouts repeated annually for progress tracking — "progress is not just hoped for but expected and achieved."

(Source: comptrain.com/gym-programming-principles)

### Weekly Template

CompTrain publishes its weekly structure explicitly:

| Day | Strength Component | Conditioning Component | Duration |
|-----|--------------------|----------------------|----------|
| **Monday** | Press (Bench or Shoulder Press) | 8–18 min Conditioning | ~60 min |
| **Tuesday** | — | 20–35 min Conditioning | ~60 min |
| **Wednesday** | Pull (Deadlift / Sumo Deadlift) | 8–18 min Conditioning | ~60 min |
| **Thursday** | — | 20–35 min Conditioning | ~60 min |
| **Friday** | Squat (Front or Back Squat) | 8–18 min Conditioning | ~60 min |
| **Saturday** | — | 20–35 min Team Workouts | ~60 min |
| **Sunday** | — | Run 2–3 miles | ~30 min |

(Source: comptrain.com/gym-programming-principles)

**Key structural patterns:**
- **3 strength days** (Mon/Wed/Fri) each paired with a shorter conditioning piece (8–18 min)
- **3 conditioning-only days** (Tue/Thu/Sat) with longer workouts (20–35 min)
- **Saturday is team day** — community-building format
- **Sunday is a dedicated run** — 2–3 miles, reinforcing running as a cornerstone
- Strength follows a **Press → Pull → Squat** rotation across the week
- **Benchmark workouts every 2 weeks** replace the scheduled conditioning piece

### Session Structure

Based on the published programming template ("Hole in the Wall"), a typical CompTrain session follows:

| Phase | Example | Duration |
|-------|---------|----------|
| Whiteboard Brief | Coach explains intent, scaling, target times | 3–5 min |
| Movement instruction | Tell, Show, Do, Check format | 5–8 min |
| Strength piece | 3 × 8 Back Squats on 3:00 clock | 12–15 min |
| Transition/Practice round | Movement rehearsal | 3–5 min |
| Conditioning piece | Every 2:00 × 5 Rounds of wallballs + DB snatches | 10–18 min |
| Post-workout cool down | Accessory/mobility/chat | 8–10 min |

**Coaching integration:** CompTrain provides detailed "Look For" coaching cues (e.g., "Flat feet — look for athletes gripping the ground with the foot throughout the rep") and specific time management guidance for class flow.

### Strength Programming Approach

CompTrain's strength work follows a notable pattern visible across months of published programming:

**Press variations (Monday):**
- Bench Press: Max Reps @80%, @90%, Heavy Set of 20, or climbing sets
- Strict Press: Max Reps, sets within 12:00 windows, 3:00 × 3 sets

**Pull variations (Wednesday):**
- Deadlift: Max Reps, 12:00 windows, climbing sets
- Sumo Deadlift: Alternates with conventional, 5-second negatives, 5–7 climbing sets

**Squat variations (Friday):**
- Back Squat: Build to Heavy Single, Max Reps @85–90%, add 10# from last attempt
- Front Squat: Max Reps @80–90%, 12:00 windows

The **"Add 10# From Last Attempt"** notation (visible in the May 10 Back Squat entry referencing 2/26/24) reveals CompTrain's long-term progressive overload tracking — the same test is repeated months later with explicit load increases.

### Representative Sample Workouts

**Workout 1: Strength + Conditioning Monday — "Hole in the Wall"**
- *Strength:* On the 3:00 × 3 Sets: 8 Back Squats — Start at 60% and build
- *Conditioning:* Every 2:00 × 5 Rounds: 25 Wall Balls (20/14 lb) + Max DB Snatches (50/35 lb)
- *Score:* Total DB Snatches
- *Scaling:* Reduce wallball reps/loading/target height as needed
- *Target pacing:* Wall balls in :60 or less, DB snatches for ~:45

**Workout 2: Long Conditioning Tuesday — "Run Up"**
- 5 Rounds For Time:
  - 400m Run
  - 6 Strict Pull-Ups
  - 400m Run
  - 15 Push-Ups
- *Total running: 4,000m (2.5 miles)*

**Workout 3: Strength + Conditioning Wednesday**
- *Strength:* Power Clean — Max Repetitions @80%
- *Conditioning — "Super Size":* 5 Rounds For Time: 10 Power Cleans (155/105 lb) + additional movements

**Workout 4: Long Conditioning Thursday**
- "Any Minute Now" — On the Minute × 20 (5 Rounds):
  - Min 1: Calorie C2 Bike
  - Min 2: Box Jumps (30/24)
  - Min 3: [Additional movement]
  - Min 4: [Additional movement]

**Workout 5: Team Saturday — "D-TEAM"**
- [Teams of 2] — 7 Rounds Each For Time:
  - 7 Deadlifts (315/205 lb)
  - 200m Sprint
  - 15 Pull-Ups
  - *Switch after full rounds*
  - Time Cap: 35 Minutes

**Workout 6: Benchmark — "Nancy"**
- 5 Rounds For Time:
  - 400m Run
  - 15 Overhead Squats (95/65 lb)

**Workout 7: Conditioning Interval**
- "Total Whine" — 10 Rounds:
  - Minute 1: Bike Erg Calories
  - Minute 2: Row Calories
  - Minute 3: Rest
  - Score: Total Calories

(Sources: comptrain.com/gym-programming, comptrain.com/programming-demo/programming-template)

### Hyrox Applicability Analysis

**Strengths — What Transfers Exceptionally Well:**

1. **Running is a cornerstone.** CompTrain is the *only* program of the three that explicitly programs running 2–3×/week plus a dedicated Sunday run of 2–3 miles. This is the single most important element for Hyrox transfer. The "Run Up" workout alone includes 4km of running with bodyweight movements between — nearly identical to Hyrox's alternating run/station format.

2. **Concurrent development model** matches Hyrox demands. Hyrox athletes need strength, endurance, and capacity simultaneously — CompTrain builds all three every week, all year. This avoids the "peaked for strength but untrained aerobically" trap.

3. **Sustainable intensity philosophy** ("build up, not burn out") aligns perfectly with Hyrox training, which requires high training volume without overtraining.

4. **No complex gymnastics** removes wasted training time. CompTrain already self-selects away from muscle-ups, handstand walks, and other CrossFit-specific skills with zero Hyrox transfer.

5. **20–35 minute conditioning pieces** (Tue/Thu/Sat) are in the right duration range for simulating portions of a Hyrox race.

6. **Team workout Saturdays** build pacing awareness and competitive energy — useful for Hyrox Doubles and race-day intensity.

7. **Benchmark testing every 2 weeks** provides the regular performance data an AI coach needs to adjust training loads.

8. **Deadlift, squat, and press strength progressions** build the base needed for sled push/pull, lunges, and wall balls.

9. **Wall balls are frequently programmed** (e.g., 25 reps in "Hole in the Wall," "Nancy" features overhead squats which share movement patterns).

10. **Rowing and Bike Erg** are standard conditioning tools (e.g., "Total Whine" with alternating row/bike intervals).

**Weaknesses — What's Missing:**

1. **Sled push/pull** is not a standard CompTrain movement — this is the single biggest gap given it's the most challenging Hyrox station for most athletes.

2. **Burpee broad jumps** are absent (CompTrain programs burpees, but not the broad jump variation specific to Hyrox).

3. **Ski erg** appears occasionally but is not programmed at race-specific distances (1km).

4. **Weighted walking lunges** at Hyrox-specific loads and distances are not a standard feature.

5. **Farmer carries** are not regularly programmed in the main class (may appear in accessories).

6. **Running is 2–3×/week, but Hyrox athletes likely need 4–5×/week** at 20–30+ km total weekly volume. The Sunday 2–3 mile run is a good start but insufficient.

7. **Power cleans and overhead squats** consume training time with limited Hyrox transfer beyond general fitness.

8. **Time-domain distribution** may skew shorter than ideal — many conditioning pieces are 8–18 min, but Hyrox race duration is 60–90+ min. More 30–45 min pieces would help.

**Modification for 16-Week Hyrox Prep:**
1. **Keep the Monday/Wednesday/Friday strength + conditioning structure** — it's excellent
2. **Replace Tuesday/Thursday conditioning with Hyrox-specific sessions:** e.g., "Hyrox simulation" workouts with 1km run + station, repeated 4× with different stations
3. **Increase Sunday run to 5–8km** and add a second dedicated run on Tuesday or Thursday
4. **Add sled work 2×/week** (push and pull at Hyrox race loads)
5. **Program Hyrox station practice as the conditioning pieces:** wall balls ×100, burpee broad jumps ×80m, farmer carry ×200m, lunges ×200m
6. **Use benchmark workouts as Hyrox-specific tests:** e.g., timed 1km row, timed 200m sled push, timed 100 wall balls
7. **Retain the concurrent development philosophy** — never drop strength entirely, but shift from max-strength testing to strength-endurance (higher reps, moderate load)

### Key Programming Principles for AI Coach Extraction

1. **Concurrent development:** Build strength, endurance, and capacity every week — never enter a "strength-only" or "endurance-only" phase
2. **Running as a non-negotiable cornerstone** at 2–3×/week minimum — the AI must include running in every weekly plan
3. **Predictable weekly structure with movement variance** — athletes should know "Monday is strength + conditioning" but the specific movements change
4. **"Intentional intensity" controls:** Movement pairings, loading, and rep schemes that create sustainable power output — the AI should calculate and cap total session volume/intensity
5. **Benchmark testing cadence:** Repeat standardized tests every 2 weeks to track progress — the AI needs a testing protocol library
6. **Program for the median athlete, not the top 10%** — the AI should default to accessible movements and scale up, not the reverse
7. **Team/partner formats** weekly for community and pacing practice
8. **Class-duration constraint** (~60 min) forces efficient session design — the AI should respect time budgets
9. **"Add weight from last attempt" progressive overload tracking** — the AI must store and reference historical performance data
10. **Detailed coaching cues per movement** ("Look For" format) — the AI should provide real-time technique reminders

---

## Cross-Program Comparative Summary

| Dimension | PRVN | HWPO | CompTrain |
|-----------|------|------|-----------|
| **Primary audience** | Affiliate classes + Hyrox athletes | Individual CrossFit athletes | Affiliate class programming |
| **Session length** | 60 min (affiliate) | ~2 hrs (Flagship) / 60 min (60) | ~60 min |
| **Weekly frequency** | 6–7 days | 5+1 active recovery + 1 rest | 6 days + Sunday run |
| **Periodization** | Named cycles, 8-week blocks | 4-week blocks, 16-week macro | Concurrent year-round |
| **Strength model** | 5-3-1 progressions | Percentage-based, high volume | Max reps at %, climbing sets |
| **Running emphasis** | Moderate (1×/week primary) | Low (bonus Zone 2) | High (2–3×/week + Sunday run) |
| **Olympic lifting** | High frequency | High frequency | Moderate (power variations) |
| **Complex gymnastics** | Yes (Ring MU, HSPU) | Yes (extensive) | No (deliberately excluded) |
| **Scaling approach** | 3 levels per WOD | Percentages + RPE | Scaling for accessibility |
| **Hyrox direct applicability** | Medium-High (has dedicated HYROX track) | Medium-Low (needs heavy modification) | Medium-High (running + conditioning focus) |
| **Best Hyrox transfer elements** | Sled work, EMOMs, HYROX track | Rowing, Zone 2, block periodization | Running volume, concurrent development, sustainability |
| **Biggest Hyrox gaps** | Running volume (affiliate track) | Running, no sled/lunge specificity | No sled work, insufficient race-length sessions |

### Synthesis: Optimal AI Coach Design Principles

Drawing from all three programs, an AI coaching system for Hyrox preparation should:

1. **Use HWPO's 4-week block periodization with deloads** (3 on / 1 deload) within a 16-week macro
2. **Adopt CompTrain's concurrent development philosophy** — never sacrifice running or endurance for a "strength phase"
3. **Follow PRVN's 60-minute session architecture** with time-blocked phases (warm-up → primer → main work → conditioning → mobility)
4. **Program running 3–4×/week minimum** (borrowing CompTrain's cornerstone principle and expanding it)
5. **Use HWPO's percentage-based loading with RPE fallback** for all strength work
6. **Implement PRVN's multi-level scaling** (3 tiers per workout) to serve athletes from beginner to advanced
7. **Design conditioning pieces in HWPO's forced-break interval format** but populate them with Hyrox-specific movements
8. **Test benchmarks every 2 weeks** (CompTrain model) using Hyrox-specific standards (1km row time, 200m sled push time, 100 wall balls time, 8km run time)
9. **Provide intent briefings** for every session (HWPO coaching video model translated to text/AI guidance)
10. **Exclude non-transferable movements** (Olympic lifts, complex gymnastics, handstand walks) in favor of Hyrox station work — following CompTrain's pragmatic movement selection philosophy

This synthesized approach captures the periodization intelligence of HWPO, the session structure and scalability of PRVN, and the sustainable conditioning philosophy and running emphasis of CompTrain — creating a purpose-built Hyrox preparation system.

### Context from: team3b_synth_20260213_084339

# Commercial Training Program Analysis for Hyrox Race Preparation

*An in-depth evaluation of three training ecosystems for applicability to Hyrox-specific AI coaching*

---

## 1. Persist by Functional Bodybuilding (Marcus Filly)

### Program Overview & Creator Background

Marcus Filly is a six-time CrossFit Games athlete and longtime CrossFit affiliate owner who pivoted his training philosophy after experiencing severe burnout and physical breakdown following the 2016 CrossFit Games. That inflection point catalyzed the creation of **Functional Bodybuilding (FBB)**, an approach that blends traditional bodybuilding hypertrophy methods with functional movement patterns, controlled tempos, and an explicit emphasis on recovery and longevity.

The flagship program, **Persist**, is a subscription-based, self-guided training platform delivered through a web-based app (Atom Training). It is not available as a native mobile app but can be bookmarked and accessed through a browser. Persist is designed for intermediate to advanced lifters—Filly and reviewers consistently note it is **not suited for true beginners** due to training volume and exercise complexity.

**Pricing:**

| Billing Cycle | Cost |
|---|---|
| Monthly | $39/month (includes 2-week free trial) |
| Quarterly | $99/quarter |
| Annual | $325/year |

**Target Audience:** Experienced lifters seeking muscle growth, improved movement quality, mobility integration, and sustainable training. Athletes transitioning away from high-intensity CrossFit-style training. Home gym owners and commercial gym users alike.

*Sources: Garage Gym Reviews Persist Review (2026); Functional Bodybuilding website; Marcus Filly YouTube channel.*

### Core Philosophy

Persist is built on several interlocking principles:

1. **Progressive Overload Through Multiple Levers:** Rather than simply adding weight to the bar each week, Persist manipulates load, repetitions, volume, rest periods, range of motion, tempo, frequency, and degree of difficulty across 6-week training cycles. As Filly states: "We typically don't use percentages of one rep maxes, but instead go by feel so that you can adapt to how you're feeling on a given day."

2. **Controlled Tempo as a Core Tool:** Tempo prescriptions appear everywhere in FBB programming. A notation like **32X1** means: 3 seconds down, 2-second hold at the bottom, eXplode up, 1-second pause at the top. This enforces movement quality, increases time under tension, and drives hypertrophy without requiring maximal loads—reducing injury risk.

3. **Structured Effort Management (RPE-Based):** Rather than fixed percentages, Persist uses RPE (Rate of Perceived Exertion) and rep ranges. For example, a squat progression might call for building across sets at RPE 6 → 7 → 8, followed by a back-off set at 80% of the top weight for max reps. This allows athletes to auto-regulate daily.

4. **Integrated Recovery:** Mobility and active recovery are not afterthoughts—they are embedded into warm-ups, cool-downs, and 2–3 dedicated mobility sessions per week. Filly's personal experience with burnout drives this emphasis on sustainable training volume.

5. **"Look Good, Move Well":** The stated goal of Persist is aesthetic and functional simultaneously—building visible muscle while maintaining (or improving) joint health, mobility, and movement competence.

*Sources: Garage Gym Reviews; Marcus Filly YouTube videos on tempo, training formats, and Pump Lift/Condition tracks.*

### Weekly Template & Training Tracks

Persist offers **five distinct tracks**, all running on **6-week training cycles** that build progressively. Athletes are encouraged to stay on one track for the full cycle. Future workouts are released one week at a time (via Sunday email previews), not all at once.

| Track | Days/Week | Session Length | Focus | Conditioning Included? |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Pillars** | 4 | ~60 min | Compound lifts (squat, bench, deadlift, OHP) + conditioning finishers | Yes (EMOMs, AMRAPs, burnout sets) |
| **Pump Condition** | 5 | ~75 min | Hypertrophy-focused lifting + conditioning at end of most sessions | Yes |
| **Pump Lift** | 5 | ~75 min | Pure hypertrophy, no conditioning | No |
| **Perform** | 5 | ~90 min | Olympic lifts + functional fitness | Yes |
| **Minimalist** | 5 | ~60 min | Minimal/no equipment workouts | Varies |

All tracks also include **2–3 dedicated mobility sessions** per week and **one full rest day**.

A typical **Pillars** weekly structure (inferred from reviewer experience and Filly's content):

| Day | Session Type |
|---|---|
| Monday | Pillars Workout A (Squat emphasis + conditioning finisher) |
| Tuesday | Mobility/Recovery |
| Wednesday | Pillars Workout B (Press emphasis + conditioning finisher) |
| Thursday | Pillars Workout C (Deadlift/Hinge emphasis + conditioning finisher) |
| Friday | Mobility/Recovery |
| Saturday | Pillars Workout D (Upper body + conditioning finisher) |
| Sunday | Full Rest |

*Note: The exact day-by-day assignment varies by cycle. From the "Persist Track Breakdown" video, we know that within Pillars, specific lifts are assigned to specific days and progress over 6 weeks (e.g., deficit deadlifts on Tuesday for 6 weeks, long pause front squats on Wednesday for weeks 1–3 transitioning to max effort work by week 6).*

*Sources: Garage Gym Reviews; Persist Track Breakdown YouTube video; Functional Bodybuilding Getting Started page.*

### Session Structure

Every Persist workout follows a consistent architecture:

1. **Warm-Up / Pre-Fatigue:** Light cardio (ski, row, run) plus movement-specific prep. Pre-fatigue targets the muscle groups of the day with higher-rep, lighter-load exercises (e.g., Bradford Z Press before a pressing session). Goal: prepare the body without fatiguing it enough to compromise the main lifts.

2. **Strength Intensity (Main Lifts):** The core of the session. Compound movements with progressive overload protocols—building sets, reverse pyramids, timed intervals, or RPE-based loading.

3. **Strength Balance (Accessories):** Supersets or agonist pairings targeting smaller muscle groups (e.g., JM Press → Inverted Skull Crushers for triceps). Higher volume, moderate intensity, shorter rest periods.

4. **Conditioning Finisher** (in applicable tracks): EMOMs, AMRAPs, or circuit-style work combining monostructural cardio with loaded movements.

5. **Hypertrophy Finisher / Cool-Down:** Drop sets, isolation work, and/or stretching/mobility.

A "Short on Time" note is provided for sessions over 60 minutes, typically reducing volume (e.g., 2 sets instead of 4) or cutting the conditioning section.

### Representative Sample Workouts

#### Sample 1: Pump Lift — Shoulders, Quads, Triceps Focus

*(From Marcus Filly's YouTube: "Muscle and Hypertrophy Workout - No Conditioning")*

| Section | Exercise | Sets × Reps | Tempo | Rest / Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Pre-Fatigue** | Ski + Row + Run (2 rounds) | 2 rounds | — | Light, blood flow |
| | Bradford Z Press | 1–2 sets × 10–15 | — | Light, mobility-focused |
| | Seated Calf Raise | 1–2 sets × 10–15 | 21X1 | — |
| **Strength Intensity 1** | Smith/DB Incline Press (75° incline) | 2 warm-up sets (15 reps, 10 reps) + 4 working sets × 8–10 | — | Every 2:00; RPE 8/10 on working sets |
| **Strength Intensity 2** | Smith/KB Front Rack Drop Lunge | Every 75 sec × 8 sets (4/leg) × 8–10 reps | — | Alternating legs; ~2 min rest per working leg |
| **Strength Balance** | JM Press → Inverted Skull Crusher (superset) | Every 3:00–3:30 × 3 sets; JM Press 5–10 reps, Skull Crusher 10–15 reps | — | 15–20 sec transition between movements |
| **Hypertrophy Finisher** | Machine Leg Extension → DB Lateral Raise (superset) | 3 sets × 12–15 + 15–20; final set: drop set to failure | — | 90 sec rest between supersets; drop 30% on last set and go to failure again |

#### Sample 2: Pump Condition — Pull Day

*(From Marcus Filly's YouTube: "Pump Condition Workout: Lift & Condition to Build More Muscle")*

| Section | Exercise | Sets × Reps | Tempo | Rest / Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Aerobic Bodybuilding** | Row 300m → Bent Over Rear Delt Fly × 10–15 → Dual KB Hang Clean High Pull × 10–15 | 4 rounds | — | Moderate pace; continuous |
| **SuperSet 1 (Strength Intensity)** | T-Bar Row 6–8 reps → Max Reps Pull-Up to Failure (switch grips each set) | Every 3:30–4:00 × 4 sets | 21X0 (T-Bar Row) | 15 sec rest between exercises; rest remainder of interval |
| **SuperSet 2 (Strength Balance)** | Incline Chest-Supported DB Elbowing Row × 12–16 → Alternating DB Curl × 16–20 (8–10/arm) | Every 90 sec × 8 total (4 sets each) | 20X0 (both) | Alternating exercises each 90 sec |
| **Conditioning** | Row 12 Cal Sprint → 6 KB Deadlifts (70 lb) → 200 ft KB Farmers Walk → 6 KB Deadlifts → 12 Body Rows | Every 3:00 × 4 sets | — | ~2 min work, ~1 min rest per round |

#### Sample 3: Back Squat Progression — Intensity + Back-Off Set

*(From Marcus Filly's YouTube: "3 Training Formats to Maximize Muscle")*

| Set | Reps | Tempo | RPE | Rest |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Warm-up sets (2–4) | Variable | 20X1 | Light | As needed |
| Working Set 1 | 6 | 20X1 | 6/10 | Every 2:30 (running clock) |
| Working Set 2 | 6 | 20X1 | 7/10 | Every 2:30 |
| Working Set 3 (Top Set) | 6 | 20X1 | 8/10 | Every 2:30 |
| Back-Off Set 4 | AMRAP | 20X0 (no pause at top or bottom—continuous tension) | Max effort | — |

*Back-Off Set uses 80% of Set 3 weight. Zero pauses between reps to maintain constant tension.*

#### Sample 4: Reverse Pyramid — Cyclist Front Squat

*(From Marcus Filly's YouTube: "3 Training Formats to Maximize Muscle")*

| Set | Reps | Tempo | Load | Rest |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Set 1 (Heaviest) | 4–6 | 30X0 | Top weight for the day | Every 2:00 |
| Set 2 | 6–8 | 30X0 | 5–10% lighter than Set 1 | Every 2:00 |
| Set 3 | 8–10 | 30X0 | 5–10% lighter than Set 2 | — |

*Progressive overload: beat Set 1 weight each time the exercise recurs (every other week in this cycle).*

#### Sample 5: Agonist Superset — Triceps

*(From Marcus Filly's YouTube: "3 Training Formats to Maximize Muscle")*

| Exercise | Sets × Reps | Tempo | Rest |
|---|---|---|---|
| JM Press | 3 × 8–10 | 30X0 | 15 sec transition to next exercise |
| DB Skull Crusher (lying tricep extension) | 3 × 12–15 | — | Rest until 3:30 mark; repeat |

*Progresses across the cycle with similar but different movements (e.g., narrow grip bench press + seated OH tricep extension the following week).*

### Hyrox Applicability Analysis

**What Transfers Well:**

- **Movement Quality & Durability:** The tempo-controlled, RPE-based approach builds resilient connective tissue and movement competency. For Hyrox athletes who need to perform sled pushes, lunges, and wall balls under extreme fatigue, this foundation of movement quality is highly transferable. Poorly executed movement under fatigue leads to time loss and injury.
- **Conditioning Integration (Pump Condition / Pillars):** The conditioning finishers—especially those combining rowing, loaded carries, kettlebell work, and bodyweight movements in timed intervals—have structural similarities to Hyrox station demands.
- **Superset & Time-Domain Training:** Persist's use of EMOM, timed supersets, and every-X-minutes formats teaches pacing under metabolic stress—a skill directly relevant to Hyrox transitions.
- **Unilateral Work & Lunge Variations:** Extensive use of single-leg work (drop lunges, split squats) directly supports the lunge station in Hyrox.
- **Farmers Carry & Loaded Movement:** Programmed regularly in conditioning sections.
- **Recovery Architecture:** The embedded mobility sessions and sustainable volume approach help prevent the overtraining that often plagues athletes trying to balance multiple training modalities.

**What's Missing:**

- **No Running Programming:** Persist has zero dedicated running. For Hyrox, where athletes run 8 × 1 km between stations, this is a critical gap. Running accounts for roughly half of total Hyrox race time.
- **No Hyrox-Specific Movements:** No sled push/pull, no wall balls, no rowing for calories (though rowing appears occasionally in conditioning), no burpee broad jumps, no ski erg intervals.
- **Limited Aerobic Base Development:** While Pump Condition includes conditioning, it is not designed to build the sustained aerobic capacity needed for a 60–75 minute Hyrox race. The conditioning is supplementary, not primary.
- **No Race-Specific Periodization:** Persist runs on continuous 6-week cycles with no taper, peak, or race-day preparation structure.

**Key Programming Principles to Extract for an AI Coach:**

1. **Tempo prescriptions as a tool for movement quality and injury prevention** (especially valuable during high-fatigue Hyrox training blocks).
2. **RPE-based loading with rep ranges** rather than fixed percentages—enables auto-regulation when combined with running fatigue.
3. **The Pre-Fatigue → Strength Intensity → Strength Balance → Conditioning Finisher session architecture** is a transferable framework.
4. **Agonist supersets for efficient volume accumulation** in time-constrained sessions.
5. **Integrated mobility as a non-negotiable** training component, not an afterthought.
6. **Progressive overload through varied stimuli** (tempo changes, range of motion, rest manipulation)—not just load increases.

---

## 2. Nick Bare's Hybrid Athlete Approach

### Creator Background

Nick Bare is a U.S. Army veteran (Infantry Platoon Leader, Ranger School graduate), founder of Bare Performance Nutrition (BPN), and arguably the most prominent figure in the hybrid athlete movement. His athletic resume includes a **2:48 marathon PR** (some sources cite 2:39), completion of the **Leadville 100-mile ultramarathon**, an **Ironman triathlon**, a **bodybuilding competition**, and a **9th place finish in the Hyrox Pro Division in Dallas** with a time of 1:05:42 (top 8% of all-time Hyrox Pro times).

Bare's origin story mirrors the hybrid athlete ethos: after leaving the military, he focused purely on bodybuilding/powerlifting and realized he was "missing something vital"—cardiovascular conditioning and functional ability. He returned to running and has spent the years since 2018 developing his methodology for combining high-volume running with serious strength training.

His philosophy: **"Hybrid athlete training is the best way to train. The reason it's the best lies directly in the results. Improved body composition, longevity, and it's sustainable."**

*Sources: Nick Bare website (nickbare.com/training); Generation Iron profile; Men's Health interview; Playbook app program listing; John Get Strong Substack analysis.*

### Training Philosophy

Bare's approach centers on several key principles:

1. **Two-a-Days as the Default:** Morning runs and evening strength training, allowing the body to recover between modalities and giving each session proper focus.

2. **Don't Add—Replace:** When adding running to a strength program, Bare advises cutting lifting from 5 days to 3 and adding 2–3 running days, rather than simply piling on more total sessions. "Whether you're just strength training or you're training hybrid, you need to start by deciding how many days you can truly commit to your workouts."

3. **Start Slow, Build Gradually:** A recommended starting point is 4 training days per week, held for at least 4 weeks before adding a 5th day or two-a-day sessions.

4. **Stimulate, Don't Obliterate:** Referenced repeatedly in his Hyrox preparation podcast (Episode 092), this principle emphasizes getting the training stimulus needed without destroying recovery capacity—critical when managing concurrent running and lifting stress.

5. **Auto-Regulation:** Bare emphasizes adjusting training based on how the body responds, especially during demanding preparation blocks.

6. **Purposeful Training:** Every session should have a clear objective. "Purpose-driven training sessions" was a key lesson from his Hyrox preparation.

*Sources: Men's Health hybrid training article; Nick Bare Podcast Episodes 092 and 100; Nick Bare website.*

### Weekly Training Structure

Nick Bare's training structure has evolved over the years depending on his current goal (marathon, ultramarathon, Hyrox, general hybrid fitness). The research data provides two distinct snapshots:

#### Current Training Split (October 2024 — Hyrox-Focused Phase)

*(From YouTube: "My Weekly Hybrid Athlete Training Split," Oct 31, 2024)*

| Day | Morning Session | Afternoon Session |
|---|---|---|
| **Monday** | 10 easy miles | Hyrox circuit training |
| **Tuesday** | — | Upper body strength + core |
| **Wednesday** | Tempo or track workout (10–12 miles) | Lower body strength |
| **Thursday** | 10 easy miles | Hyrox circuit training |
| **Friday** | ~8 easy miles | Upper body strength + core |
| **Saturday** | Long run + accessory work | — |
| **Sunday** | 8–10 easy miles | — |

**Weekly running mileage: ~65 miles/week**

This is an extremely high-volume training schedule reflecting Bare's advanced fitness level and years of progressive base building. The structure reveals several important design choices:

- **Easy runs dominate:** 4 of the 6 running days are easy-pace efforts, consistent with the 80/20 polarized training model.
- **Only one quality run session per week:** The Wednesday tempo/track workout is the sole high-intensity running session.
- **Hyrox circuits appear twice weekly:** Monday and Thursday afternoons, providing sport-specific preparation.
- **Strength training 3× per week:** Upper/upper/lower split, prioritizing the sessions that support Hyrox performance.
- **Sunday as a "recovery run" day:** Not a full rest day, but a lower-volume easy run without afternoon lifting.

#### Hybrid Athlete 1.0 Program (General Hybrid Training Template)

*(From Playbook app listing)*

| Day | AM Session | PM Session |
|---|---|---|
| **Day 1** | Easy Run | Push Strength |
| **Day 2** | Easy Run | Pull Strength |
| **Day 3** | Interval Run | Lower Body Strength |
| **Day 4** | Optional Aerobic Workout | Dedicated Mobility |
| **Day 5** | Threshold Run | Upper Body Hypertrophy |
| **Day 6** | Rest | Dedicated Mobility |
| **Day 7** | Easy Run | Lower Body Hypertrophy |

**Key differences from the Hyrox-focused split:** 5 weight training sessions vs. 3; 5 running workouts vs. 6–7; 2 dedicated mobility days; no sport-specific circuit work. This represents a more balanced, general-purpose hybrid template with roughly equal emphasis on strength and running.

#### Marathon Training Block Periodization

*(From Nebraska Food Cooperative PDF)*

Bare's marathon plans typically span **16–20 weeks** with the following structure:

- **Weekly mileage:** Starts at 15–20 miles/week, builds to 40–50 miles/week at peak (weeks 12–14).
- **Long runs:** Progressive, increasing ~10% per week, peaking at 20–22 miles before a taper.
- **3 quality runs per week:** Track repeats (400m/800m intervals), tempo runs (75–85% max HR), and the long run.
- **2 aerobic cross-training days:** Swimming, rowing, or stationary bike for endurance without running impact.
- **Taper phase:** Reduced volume in final 2–3 weeks before race day.

### Representative Sample Workouts / Training Days

#### Sample Day 1: Hyrox-Phase Monday (Inferred from Oct 2024 Split)

| Time | Session | Details |
|---|---|---|
| 5:00 AM | Easy Run | 10 miles at conversational pace |
| PM | Hyrox Circuit | Sled push, sled pull, wall balls, burpee broad jumps, farmers carry, rowing — sport-specific preparation (exact prescriptions not publicly available) |

#### Sample Day 2: Pull Strength (from Hybrid Athlete 1.0 / Generation Iron)

| Exercise | Sets × Reps | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Pull-Ups | 4 × AMRAP | Bodyweight |
| Deadlifts | 3 × 5 | Heavy — heaviest possible with good form |
| Lat Pulldowns | 4 × 8 | Superset format noted in BPN Training app |
| Pendlay Rows | 4 × 12 | — |
| Low Rows | 4 × 10 | — |
| Dumbbell Rows | 4 × 10 | — |

#### Sample Day 3: Chest Workout (from Generation Iron)

| Exercise | Sets × Reps | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| *Pre-Workout:* Concept2 Bike | 3 sets | Light; plus resistance band stretches, light DB rotations |
| Bench Press | 4 × 8 | Heavy |
| Incline Dumbbell Press | 4 × 5 | Heavy |
| Superset: Seated Cable Fly + Push-Ups | 4 × 8 / 4 × AMRAP | 60–90 sec rest between supersets |
| Bodyweight Dips | 4 × 10 | — |

|---|---|---|
| Leg Extensions | 4 × 12 | Warm-up / pre-fatigue |

#### Sample Day 5: Long Run Day (Saturday, from multiple sources)

| Component | Details |
|---|---|
| Long Run | 15–22 miles depending on training phase; progressive increase ~10%/week |
| Pacing | Conversational for most; possible progression to marathon pace in final miles |
| Accessory Work | Light accessory/mobility work post-run |

*Note: Bare's Hyrox-specific circuit workout details are referenced in podcast episodes 092 and 100 but the exact exercise prescriptions, sets, reps, and rest periods are not publicly documented in the research data. The circuits are known to include sled push, sled pull, wall balls, burpee broad jumps, farmers carry, and rowing, mirroring the Hyrox race format.*

### Hyrox Applicability Analysis

**Nick Bare's hybrid model is arguably the closest existing public training template to what a Hyrox athlete needs.** His Hyrox Pro debut performance (1:05:42, 9th of 207 in Pro Division) validates the approach.

**What Transfers Directly:**

- **High Aerobic Base:** 65 miles/week of running provides an enormous aerobic engine. Hyrox is fundamentally an aerobic event lasting 60–90 minutes, and Bare's running volume builds exactly the metabolic capacity needed.
- **Two-a-Day Structure:** The AM run / PM strength (or circuit) model maps directly onto Hyrox preparation, allowing sport-specific work and base building in the same day.
- **Concurrent Strength + Endurance:** Bare has years of experience managing the interference effect between strength and endurance training. His solutions (separating sessions by 6+ hours, prioritizing recovery, auto-regulating intensity) are directly applicable.
- **Hyrox Circuit Sessions:** Twice-weekly sport-specific circuits directly target the 8 Hyrox functional stations.
- **Race Periodization Experience:** Bare has periodized for marathons (16–20 week blocks with progressive overload and taper), Ironman, and ultramarathons. This periodization knowledge translates to Hyrox race preparation.
- **Mental Toughness & Pacing:** Bare's "stimulate, don't obliterate" philosophy and emphasis on purposeful training help prevent the overtraining that commonly derails Hyrox preparation.

**What Could Be Improved for Hyrox:**

- **Running Volume May Be Excessive:** 65 miles/week is far beyond what most Hyrox athletes need. Hyrox involves only 8 km total running. The high mileage reflects Bare's marathon background rather than Hyrox optimization. A more Hyrox-specific approach might reduce running to 25–40 miles/week and add more erg work (rowing, ski erg) and functional station practice.
- **Strength Training Volume is Reduced:** In the Hyrox phase, Bare lifts only 3×/week (2 upper, 1 lower). For sled push/pull performance, which demands significant lower body and posterior chain strength, additional lower body strength work could be beneficial.
- **Hyrox-Specific Weaknesses Identified:** As the John Get Strong analysis noted, Bare lost time on sled pull, burpees, rowing, and wall balls—the more technical Hyrox-specific movements. More dedicated practice with these movements (beyond twice-weekly circuits) could improve performance.
- **Public Program Lacks Specificity:** While Bare's personal training is well-documented via YouTube, the publicly available Hybrid Athlete 1.0 program on Playbook is a general hybrid template—it does not include Hyrox-specific work.

**Key Programming Principles to Extract for an AI Coach:**

1. **AM/PM split for concurrent training** — separate running and strength by maximum time to minimize interference.
2. **Polarized running distribution** — mostly easy runs with 1–2 quality sessions per week.
3. **Progressive mileage building** — 10% weekly increase, 16–20 week macrocycles, taper before competition.
4. **"Stimulate, don't obliterate"** — manage training stress holistically across both modalities.
5. **Auto-regulation as standard practice** — adjust based on recovery status, not rigid adherence to plan.
6. **Sport-specific circuit training** — dedicate 2 sessions/week to practicing actual race movements in race-like conditions.
7. **Four-day minimum starting point** for hybrid beginners, building to 5–6 days over 4+ weeks.
8. **Strength training uses traditional bodybuilding rep schemes** (4 × 8–12 with heavy loads) — simple, proven, effective.

---

## 3. BPN (Bare Performance Nutrition) Community Training

### Program Overview

Bare Performance Nutrition (BPN) is primarily a sports nutrition and supplement company founded by Nick Bare. In **February 2023**, BPN launched the **BPN Training app**, expanding beyond supplements into structured fitness programming. The app was positioned as a free, community-oriented training tool—a significant differentiator in a market dominated by paid programs.

**Key Details:**

|---|---|
| **Cost** | Free (unlimited access to all programming) |
| **Programs Available** | 4 programs: Hybrid Athlete, 5K, Half Marathon, Marathon |

| **Platform** | Mobile app (BPN Training) |
| **Integration** | Garmin Connect compatibility for health/fitness data syncing |
| **Content** | Exercise library with video demonstrations, educational articles on fitness and nutrition |

*Sources: BusinessWire press release (Feb 2023); Silicon UK press release; BPN website; BPN Training app listing.*

### Training Philosophy

BPN Training's philosophy extends directly from Nick Bare's personal training ethos, packaged for broader accessibility:

- **"Go One More":** BPN's motivational tagline, encouraging athletes to push beyond perceived limits.
- **"Prove Yourself Right":** A 2023 campaign encouraging commitment to physically challenging goals.
- **Personalization:** Programs adapt based on fitness data (via Garmin Connect integration), adjusting to the user's fitness level over time.
- **Accessibility:** The decision to make all programming free reflects a philosophy that quality training should not be gated behind paywalls. As Nick Bare stated: "There aren't great training programs available that provide personalized, quality resources at no cost."
- **Holistic Approach:** BPN Training encompasses not just workouts but also nutritional guidance, recovery strategies, and mental well-being components.

### Available Programming

The four programs represent a progression from running-specific to hybrid:

1. **5K Program** (12–16 weeks): Entry-level running program for beginners building toward a 5K race.
2. **Half Marathon Program** (12–16 weeks): Intermediate running progression.
3. **Marathon Program** (12–16 weeks): Advanced marathon preparation following Nick Bare's methodology.
4. **Hybrid Athlete Program** (12–16 weeks): The flagship program combining running and strength training—structurally similar to the Hybrid Athlete 1.0 program available on Playbook.

The Hybrid Athlete program on BPN Training follows a **Push/Pull/Lower** strength training split combined with running workouts. From the limited public footage available (YouTube: "First pull workout of the Hybrid Training Program on the new BPN Training App"), we know:

- Workouts include supersets (e.g., lat pulldown superset with low rows on pull day).
- The app provides supplement recommendations tied to each workout (e.g., Endo Pump and Flight pre-workout for a pull session).
- Exercise demonstrations with detailed instructions are provided within the app.

- **Scalability:** Programs include beginner and intermediate/advanced versions for running workouts.

### Hyrox Applicability Analysis

**What Transfers:**

- **Hybrid Athlete Framework:** The BPN Hybrid Athlete program provides a solid general template for concurrent strength and running training—the foundation of any Hyrox preparation program.
- **Free Access + Garmin Integration:** The zero-cost model and Garmin Connect compatibility make it an accessible entry point for athletes exploring hybrid training.
- **Running Program Expertise:** The 5K, Half Marathon, and Marathon programs demonstrate structured running periodization knowledge that supports the aerobic development needed for Hyrox.
- **Community & Accountability:** The social/community features support long-term adherence.

**What's Missing — A Significant Gap:**

- **No Hyrox-Specific Programming:** As of the available data, BPN Training does not offer a Hyrox-specific program. The four available programs (Hybrid Athlete, 5K, Half Marathon, Marathon) do not include sled push/pull, wall balls, burpee broad jumps, ski erg, or any of the 8 Hyrox functional fitness stations.
- **Limited Public Workout Detail:** Despite being free, the full workout prescriptions are only visible within the app itself. The research data does not provide enough detail to fully evaluate the quality of the programming (tempo prescriptions, progressive overload structure, periodization model).
- **No Conditioning/Functional Fitness Integration:** The Hybrid Athlete program appears to separate running and strength training cleanly—there is no equivalent to Persist's conditioning finishers or Bare's Hyrox circuit sessions.
- **General-Purpose Design:** The programs are designed for broad accessibility, not competition-specific preparation. This makes them valuable for building a base but insufficient for direct Hyrox preparation.

**Key Programming Principles to Extract for an AI Coach:**

1. **Free, accessible programming as an onboarding mechanism** — lower barriers to entry for beginners.
2. **Garmin Connect / wearable integration** for adaptive programming based on real physiological data.
3. **Scaled programming versions** (beginner vs. intermediate/advanced) within the same program structure.
4. **Supplement integration as a value-add** (relevant for a commercial coaching product, though secondary to training quality).
5. **Push/Pull/Lower split** as a proven, simple strength training framework for hybrid athletes.

## Comparative Summary: Hyrox Readiness Matrix

| Dimension | Persist (Filly) | Nick Bare Hybrid | BPN Training |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Running Development** | ❌ None | ✅✅✅ Elite-level (65 mi/wk) | ✅✅ Structured programs (5K–Marathon) |

| **Beginner-Friendly** | ❌ Not recommended | ✅ Scaled versions available | ✅✅ Designed for all levels |

## Synthesis: Key Principles for an AI Hyrox Coach

Drawing across all three programs, the following principles emerge as foundational for an AI coaching system targeting Hyrox preparation:

1. **Concurrent Training Architecture (from Bare):** AM/PM splits separating running from strength/circuits; polarized running distribution (80% easy / 20% quality); progressive mileage building with taper.

2. **Movement Quality & Tempo Control (from Filly):** Tempo prescriptions for injury-proofing and muscle development; RPE-based auto-regulation rather than fixed percentages; structured session architecture (warm-up → main lift → accessories → conditioning).

3. **Sport-Specific Circuit Integration (from Bare's Hyrox phase):** 2× weekly Hyrox-specific circuit sessions practicing actual race movements (sled push/pull, wall balls, burpee broad jumps, farmers carry, rowing, ski erg) in race-simulated conditions.

4. **Progressive Overload Through Multiple Variables (from Filly):** Load, reps, tempo, rest, range of motion, and exercise complexity as independent levers for progression—not just weight on the bar.

5. **Recovery as a First-Class Training Component (from Filly + Bare):** Dedicated mobility sessions, embedded warm-up/cool-down protocols, and the "stimulate, don't obliterate" philosophy to manage the uniquely high demands of concurrent training.

6. **Adaptive Scaling (from BPN):** Programming that adjusts to user fitness level, with beginner/intermediate/advanced versions of the same framework, enabled by wearable data integration.

7. **Periodization for Race Day (from Bare):** 16–20 week macrocycles with progressive volume building, peak training at weeks 12–14, and a structured taper phase—adapted from marathon methodology to suit the Hyrox competitive calendar.

An effective AI Hyrox coach would synthesize Filly's session design sophistication and movement quality emphasis with Bare's concurrent training framework and race periodization experience, while incorporating the accessibility and adaptive scaling principles demonstrated by BPN Training. The critical addition that none of these programs fully provides is a **purpose-built Hyrox periodization model** that systematically develops all 8 functional stations alongside the running demands, progressing from general physical preparation through sport-specific training to race-day peaking.
